Official Telegram

Zhenjiang Telegram to All Newspapers: Jiangsu Province has suffered from torrential rains since the beginning of summer this year, causing severe flooding of farmlands in various districts, leading to the near-total loss of the autumn harvest. In addition, the Grand Canal has risen, and the sea dikes have collapsed. Disaster reports have been received from more than fifty counties, accounting for nine-tenths of the province. Unexpectedly, a hurricane suddenly arose this month, with torrential rains causing the canal dikes to be impossible to protect, resulting in the collapse of dozens of sections. Huge floods rushed downwards, turning the counties downstream along the canal into a sea, drowning countless people. Floating corpses follow the waves in an endless stream. Only the strong managed to climb onto rooftops or tree tops, crying for rescue. This unprecedented catastrophe is the worst in a century. This government

has dispatched numerous officials with boats, carrying dry rations, to provide rescue in different directions. Meanwhile, reception centers have been set up to provide emergency relief. However, the disaster area is vast, and the number of people is large. Relying solely on government funds for assistance is like a drop in the bucket. We hope that people from all walks of life will have compassion, donate righteous grain, and act quickly with a sense of urgency to alleviate hunger and prevent drowning. Contribute generously, either through donations or by raising large sums of money. Expand the scope of public assistance and provide aid like that of Chunren's wheat boat. This would be an act of life-saving grace, more than just providing temporary relief. On behalf of the disaster victims, we respectfully implore you. Jiangsu Provincial Government.　　Zhenjiang Telegram to All Newspapers: According to the report from the commissioner sent to Shaobo for disaster relief, fifteen sections of the Shaobo dike have collapsed. The main dam at Zhaoguan has not collapsed, but there is a gap of more than a zhang (about 10 feet) north of the dam. Currently, the water is gradually receding, about four chi (about 4 feet) below the dike. The people affected by the disaster are unwilling to leave Shaobo, and their food supplies have been lost, leaving them in urgent need of food. We still hope that all parties will continue to provide urgent relief. Officials have also been dispatched to Gaoyou, Shixing, Dongtai, Yanfu, and other counties to distribute grain. Disaster reports will be continued as they are received. Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs.　　Zhenjiang Telegram to Shenbao Newspaper for Relay to Compatriots from Yancheng, Fudong, Taixing, and Xinghua Counties in Shanghai: In recent days, the canal dikes north of the Yangtze River have collapsed in eighteen places, causing the waters of the Huai and Yangtze to rush directly into the lower reaches. In an instant, graves and houses were submerged. Floating corpses are visible everywhere. This is even worse than the Qingshuitan breach during the Tongzhi era (1862-1874). Those clinging on awaiting rescue have already been doing so for several days. Although the provincial government has requisitioned boats for rescue, it is like a drop in the bucket and of little help. We plan to implore fellow countrymen in Shanghai to quickly form groups to request relief from disaster relief organizations. At the same time, we request the government to immediately close the breaches to prevent permanent submersion and irrecoverable devastation. We earnestly pray. Disaster Relief Association of Yancheng, Fudong, Taixing, and Xinghua stationed in Zhenjiang.　　Zhenjiang Telegram Urgent: Shanghai Shenbao Newspaper to the Jiangning Fellow Association of Zhenjiang in Shanghai: The day before yesterday, there was a fierce wind and heavy rain that did not stop all night. Coupled with the sudden rise of the Yangtze River tide, the south bank of Shunjiangzhou collapsed for more than ten zhang (about 100 feet), submerging more than a dozen large and small dikes such as Dongxi and Huanyuan. Hundreds of households were affected by the disaster, with more than three thousand people affected. The number of deaths is currently under investigation. Currently, the victims are sheltering on the riverbank, exposed to the wind and dew, in extreme misery. In addition to making every effort to close the breach and provide relief, we implore our fellow countrymen to consider the disaster situation in their hometown and generously provide urgent relief so that thousands of victims can be spared from waiting for death. Then, the merit will be immeasurable. Please remit donations directly to Mr. Tao Jianming of Yulong Bank in Zhenjiang for unified distribution. With this urgent telegram, we cannot express our gratitude and anticipation. Liu Lianchen, Commander of the Seventh District Security Group, Zhenjiang County.

Yangzhou Telegram to All Newspapers: It is found that this flood is an unprecedented catastrophe, and Jiangsu is a province with many waters, with rivers crisscrossing and lakes scattered like stars. Overflowing torrents cause particularly severe damage. The people affected along the Yangtze River and the Huai River cannot be counted. Recently, in Shaobo Town, Jiangdu, the canal dike collapsed, and thousands more people were buried in the bellies of fish. According to a telegram from the town's business and agricultural association, Shaobo is unfortunate, with disasters occurring in succession. After the ravages of war in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927), the seventeenth and eighteenth years (1928-1929) suffered severe droughts, causing families to be separated and scarred everywhere. In the nineteenth year (1930), there was finally a harvest, and we hoped to accumulate resources and recover, hoping to be rescued. Unexpectedly, Heaven did not have mercy, and this year's flood descended again, turning fields, graves, and residences into a swamp. Considering that Shaobo has suffered seven calamities of water, drought, and war, the people's wealth has been exhausted. When disaster strikes, the suffering is greater than in other towns. Our benevolent director has personally witnessed the tragic disaster in Yangzhou. On behalf of the town, he telegraphed Shanghai's charitable organizations, asking for aid and compassion. The situation in our town is already well known, so there is no need to elaborate. We hereby telegraph the director again, continuing to telegraph all parties, to provide relief funds as soon as possible, so that one day's earlier relief will alleviate one day's hardship, and save one more person's life, etc. Zhijiang (Zhang Zhijiang) is in charge of soothing this state, and it is difficult to sit idly by. We have previously telegraphed various charitable organizations to give assistance for rescue. Now, we respectfully implore on behalf of countless disaster victims, asking all charitable organizations and philanthropists to consider the plight of the disaster victims who are crying out for food and generously donate righteous grain and benevolent soup, so that these descendants can celebrate their rebirth. Then, not only will those who receive the rain and dew feel great gratitude, but also Zhijiang will sincerely pray and bow incessantly. With urgent telegrams, we cannot express our expectations. Zhang Zhijiang respectfully.

Yangzhou Telegram to All Newspapers: It is learned that the disaster relief personnel sent by Director Zhang Zhijiang to Gaoyou returned last night on the Junliang and Tongyu steamers, carrying more than a thousand disaster victims, who were handed over to Changsheng Temple for reception. This morning, Adviser Zhang Daorong and more than ten other officials were dispatched again, carrying ships and relief supplies to the Gaoyou area for a second round of rescue. Jiangsu Pacification Director's Office.

Important News

All Parties Pay Attention to the Flood in Northern Jiangsu 67

Zhenjiang Merchants Request Maintaining Finance. The export of Zhenjiang's goods relies heavily on the counties north of the Yangtze River. The financial sector's loans are also concentrated in the north. Commercial transactions are settled three times a year, while financial transactions are settled at the end of the year. The counties north of the Yangtze primarily absorb goods and capital from Zhenjiang, followed by Nanjing and Yangzhou. The breaches at Gaoyou and Shaobo have resulted in the complete submergence of the commercial center of Gaoyou, outside the North Gate, and the entire town of Shaobo. The water in Xinghua is level with the eaves. Dongtai, Funing, Baoying, Sishui, and Yancheng are also in critical condition. If the dikes breach again, the above-mentioned areas may be unsafe. Qingjiang and Huaian counties, due to their downstream location, are likely safe. The counties affected by the disaster owe Zhenjiang merchants and financial institutions no less than several million dollars. Zhenjiang's commerce has already been in a severe decline this year. Having suffered this setback, business is undoubtedly impacted, and the loans extended are even more difficult to recover. After hearing the warnings, all merchants are showing their worries. Chairman Lu Xiaobo of the Chamber of Commerce, in view of this, yesterday made a presentation to Chairman Ye of the provincial government, requesting the provincial government to provide special maintenance for the financial sector in the disaster area, in addition to emergency relief, rescue, and accommodation. After the flood recedes, the markets in the counties and cities north of the Yangtze can be easily restored, and the losses to Zhenjiang can be reduced. Chairman Ye and the provincial committee members agreed and have promised to assist.

The Northern Jiangsu Water Conservancy and Post-Disaster Construction Bureau yesterday sent engineer Zhang Bin as a special commissioner for rescue, accompanied by Xiang Kaiti, Zuo Yingshi, and engineering personnel, carrying a large amount of materials, to the breaches at Gaoyou and Shaobo to block them. The Security Bureau also dispatched four companies of soldiers to assist, and they also set off together. It also ordered Dafeng and Yuhua companies to quickly dredge eight hundred zhang (about 8,000 feet) of the Zhongmao Youdong end to connect to Wangjiagang and discharge water into the sea. As for the water conservancy and post-disaster funds, the provincial government has decided to transfer 1.14 million yuan from the Guayu Provincial Highway project designated in the construction bonds to water conservancy and post-disaster, and allocate a portion to handle work relief and 500,000 yuan for the construction of the Sheyang River gate as funds for rescue and repair.

Shanghai Gentry Prepare to Distribute Relief. After the dike breach at Gaoyou and Shaobo, Chairman Lu Xiaobo of the Chamber of Commerce, in addition to actively raising relief funds, also telegraphed the Shanghai Jiangsu Flood Relief Association, requesting the allocation of funds for relief. Yesterday, Wang Yiting, Cheng Jingsheng, and others replied by telegram, asking to prepare ten steamboats, thirty tugboats, 5,000 catties of large cakes, 50,000 steamed buns each from Jingjiang, and 6,000 rush mats for distribution in the disaster area. Cheng Jingsheng arrived in Zhenjiang this morning and plans to personally inspect the area. It is also heard that Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs has urgently telegraphed Yizheng, Wuxian, Changshu, Wuxi, Wujin, and other counties to requisition steamboats and tugboats, which the respective county governments will send with officials, arriving at the province for concentration before the 28th, for use in rescuing disaster victims in the disaster area.

Yangzhou Handles Emergency Relief After Shaobo Dike Collapses 68

Yangzhou Correspondence: Responsible persons of various agencies and organizations in Jiangdu, and local people, held a meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce at 10 AM on the 28th to discuss post-disaster measures. County Magistrate Chen presided over the meeting, reporting on the disaster situation along the Shaobo dike and the process of requesting funds from the province and dispatching wheels for rescue, and said that he had ordered the Public Security Bureau to seal and hire twenty civilian boats to rescue and assist in the disaster area, and to arrange the locations for reception centers: (1) Datong Flour Company outside Dongguan; (2) Changsheng Temple outside the breach; (3) Puzhao Temple outside Xuningmen; (4) Xu Gongci outside Guangchumen. Then, Dai Tianqiu reported on the disaster situation, saying that the disaster area on the east bank of Shaobo was the most extensive, and it was not easy for the boats going to rescue the disaster victims in various villages to enter the area. Efforts must be made to find a solution, and everyone was asked to donate money. The attendees pledged to donate 1,730 yuan. Then, Wu Zunyi reported that the boats had been properly contacted with the director's office. Subsequently, the method of organizing the Jiangdu Flood Emergency Relief Committee was discussed: (1) Ten people, including County Magistrate Chen and Wang Jingting, were selected as standing committee members, and twenty people, including Hu Xianbo, were selected as committee members, divided into general affairs, reception, and distribution sections; (2) Ruan Lianzhong was appointed to be responsible for salvaging corpses; (3) The meeting place was attached to the Chamber of Commerce. Afterwards, a standing committee meeting was held, and Wang Jingting and Dai Tianqiu were elected as chairman and vice-chairman to allocate responsibilities, and nine items were discussed and resolved. The meeting adjourned.

Tragic Situation in Disaster Area and Relief Efforts. After the Shaobo dike collapsed, the large and small towns and villages within a radius of fifteen li (about 5 miles), as well as Qiaoye Dingjiahuo and other places, were all destroyed. In addition to waiting for rescue by climbing on roofs and trees, the corpses of men and women, as well as boxes, furniture, cattle, dogs, livestock, etc., floated on the water surface, which was shocking to see. Just in Chenjiaqiao and Jiangjiayuan and other places on the Yunyan River, which connects Shaobo and Tongxian, the boxes and utensils salvaged by the villagers were piled up like mountains. Many people, including Zhu Xiaoliuzi and others, fell into the water and drowned while trying to salvage objects. Countless floating corpses flowed from the Jinwan River into the area under the Wanfu Bridge and Yanjiabridge. Dozens of corpses have been salvaged in Yanjiabridge alone. On the 28th, the water in Shaobo Town had receded, and the depth was only up to the ankles. The number of deaths and injuries was estimated to be more than a thousand. There were even more deaths in nearby towns and villages. The floating corpses and objects in the river from Wantou to Xianzhen were like ants. Unfortunately, people were fighting to salvage objects, while the corpses were allowed to drift with the waves, and no one could take care of them. As of the evening of the 28th, more than a thousand disaster victims rescued had arrived in Yangzhou and were sent to various reception centers for resettlement. Officials, the Director's Office, the Red Swastika Society, and the Chamber of Commerce sent ships to rescue the disaster, and loaded food to distribute to the disaster area. Chairman Wang Jingting also boarded the ship northward at 4 PM.

Provincial Order Sealing Firewood and Straw. The county government was ordered by the provincial government to seal all firewood sheds and existing firewood stacks within the county to be used for dike construction. As a result, the fuel supply for shops throughout the city was greatly panicked, and the coal shops' profits were tenfold.

Investigation of Danger Areas in Northern Jiangsu. The canal dike north of the Yangtze River has been in danger in many sections due to the strong winds and heavy rain on the 25th and 26th. The investigation is as follows: (1) Six gates in three places; (2) One place at Jimaozhou, about forty zhang (about 400 feet); (3) Eight places in the southern section of Shaobo; (4) Fifteen zhang (about 150 feet) south of the Wanshou Palace; (5) More than ten zhang (about 100 feet) north of the Wanshou Palace; (6) Dozens of zhang (about 100 feet) at the Sanyuan Temple of the Sancao Gate; (7) Dozens of zhang (about 100 feet) in two places at the Hehuatang; (8) Thirty zhang (about 300 feet) north of the Laishou Nunnery; (9) A steep slope in the inner slope north of the Chenghuang Temple; (10) A steep slope in the northern part of Hehuatang, dozens of zhang (about 100 feet); (11) A steep slope in Ciajiatan, dozens of zhang (about 100 feet); (12) Part of the Longwang Temple was unloaded; (13) Dozens of zhang (about 100 feet) of the west slope of Caijiatan were unloaded; (14) The ancient Zhaoguan Dam was steep and cracked; also, the Lihuo Straight Dam at the Honghu Weiyi River section of the Huaishao section of the canal dike was breached by a hundred zhang (about 1,000 feet), and five water diversion dams were all washed away. The stone work of the Honghu Dam was also partially collapsed and is being protected.

Li Mingyang Reports on the Disaster in Shao and You. Li Mingyang, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Department, went to northern Jiangsu from Zhenjiang yesterday for inspection. He arrived in Yangzhou at about 9 PM that night and telegraphed the province, stating that, according to Brigade Commander Xu's report, more than ten sections of the Shaobo Dike had collapsed, and the entire town was flooded, with many deaths and injuries. Also, according to Chen, the county magistrate of Jiangdu, the water in Shaobo Town was several chi (about several feet) deep, and people were climbing trees and roofs, urgently awaiting rescue. Also, according to Ma Boliang, a refugee from Gaoyou who had escaped to Yangzhou, the Yu Matou Dike breached at night the day before yesterday, drowning countless people and animals. The northwest, east, and south gates of Gaoyou were blocked, and the north gate water gate was being urgently blocked. The residents' cries for help were extremely tragic, etc. In addition to instructing County Magistrate Chen to quickly find a way to rescue them, he requested that more boats be sealed and hired in Zhenjiang to carry food to rescue them, etc. It is also heard that hundreds of large and small boats along the river in Gaoyou were all stopped near the North Gate to load and unload wheat flour and grain. Due to the excessive wind and waves, all the boats suffered disasters and sank. The water in Gaoyou City is now four chi (about four feet) deep, and the disaster situation is quite serious.

The handling by the Pacification Office. The Jiangsu Pacification Director's Office convened an emergency meeting of senior officials last night and decided to send Councilor Zhang Ruitang, leading aides and more than fifty guards, to immediately hire two steamboats and a total of twenty-five civilian boats of various sizes, carrying more than 10,000 catties of food, to rush to the disaster area overnight to implement the rescue of the distressed people, and to telegraph General Commander Liang and the brigade commander stationed in Yangzhou to carry out the same actions, and to send teams to protect the river dikes and block the breaches to prevent them from collapsing further.

Northern Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Holds Meeting 69

Cheng Jingsheng Reports on Relief Efforts

Decided to Elect the Association's Officers

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Northern Jiangsu Flood Relief Association held its first meeting at 10 AM on the 29th in the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce Auditorium. The attendees included Qian Shuchu, Zhou Daoqian, Sun Xingwu, Hu Jicheng, Zhang Yiyun, Zhang Zuwu, Liu Jianxing, Huo Zenghua, Cai Yunsun, Fang Shaozhi, Yang Guangyu, Yang Gongya, Xie Yuqiu, Wu Jiheng, Lu Runzhou, Cheng Futao, Zhou Zigeng, Yu Xiaochuan, Hu Jianchun, Yan Junfu, Leng Yuqiu, and Lu Xiaobo. Cheng Jingsheng reported that the association had received reports of disasters in thirteen counties. Because the disaster situation in each county was extremely serious, the Jiangsu Provincial Government specifically entrusted the association to handle flood relief matters in each county. I am here in Zhenjiang this time, authorized by four organizations, the National Government Relief Committee, the Shanghai Provincial Flood Relief Association, the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association, and the Jiangsu Provincial Relief Committee. The emergency relief areas are Jiangpu, Tongshan, Dongtai, Gaoyou, Baoying, Lianshui, Ganyu, Yangzhou Liyang, Jintan, Zhenjiang, Jiangdu, and Liuhe. Hunan Province's Flood Relief Plan 70

A total of fifty-four counties in the province were affected by the disaster

More than 12 million disaster victims

Five or six million mu of fields were flooded

Changsha Correspondence: The flood disaster in Hunan Province this year is severe, unprecedented in decades. The extent of the disaster area reaches fifty-four counties, accounting for more than two-thirds of the province's seventy-five counties. More than five hundred people died from drowning, more than 200,000 houses were destroyed, and five to six million mu of fields were flooded. Four-tenths of the people in the province were affected by the disaster, with an estimated 12 million disaster victims. People from all walks of life in the province are rushing to call for relief. Therefore, flood relief is the most serious issue in Hunan Province at present. Party and government leaders have telegraphed the Central Government to list Hunan Province as a first-class disaster area and to issue urgent relief funds as soon as possible, and have telegraphed American philanthropists to ask for assistance. Meanwhile, Wang Qi and Yuan Jiapu were appointed as representatives to go to Beijing and Shanghai to solicit funds. The Hunan Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, the Provincial Relief Committee, and the Hunan Flood Relief Research Association are paying close attention to flood relief. He Jian has convened six meetings in recent days to formulate detailed plans to treat both the symptoms and the root causes, and they were submitted to the joint party and government meeting on the 22nd for approval and implementation. The content of the plan includes maintaining food supply, raising relief funds, and regulating food supply as measures to treat the symptoms, and implementing water conservancy as a measure to treat the root causes. It is expected that they will be implemented separately in the near future. (August 23)

Chiang Returns to Jiangxi 72

Military Operations Against Bandits: Situation Report 73

Chairman Chiang and Soong Mei-ling Return to Nanchang

Anti-Red Army Operations Conducted in Divisions

Bounty for Bandit Leaders Increased by 50,000 Yuan

Nanchang Dispatch: Commander-in-Chief Chiang departed Nanchang on the 16th evening aboard the warship "Chu You" for Nanjing, then Shanghai. On the 23rd, around 8 PM, he returned to Nanchang on the same ship with his wife, Soong Mei-ling. Welcoming him at the riverbank were Chief of Staff Xiong of the Headquarters, various department heads, Governor Lu of the Provincial Government, and other dignitaries. After disembarking, Chiang went directly to the Headquarters, while Soong stayed at the residence of missionary Mr. Ge Xingren of the St. James' Episcopal Church near Lingying Bridge. Yesterday, Shangguan Yunxiang, Lu Diping, Hu Zongnan, and others went to the Headquarters to request instructions on future anti-Red strategies.

Since the beginning of the month, Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and Huang Gonglue have mobilized all their forces for resistance. From Gu Po Sha Village in Taihe, east through Yongfeng Xuqiao and Qiaotou in Xingguo, Yindu Yinkeng and Datian, Yongfeng Liangcun Junbu and Longgang Xu, Ningdu Wangpi and Xiaobu, to the Kutao Qianshan area on the southern border of Guangchang, there have been constant fierce battles between the National Army and the Red bandits. The Red bandits have suffered repeated heavy blows, so they have hidden in deep mountains and remote valleys. According to those familiar with military affairs and bandit activity, the Red bandits' strategy consists of two points: (1) Whenever they see National Army units that are weak, they concentrate their main forces in one location, hoping to seize weapons. (2) If they see that the National Army has a strong force, they absolutely avoid contact, not firing a single shot or shell. Now the National Army has seen through their tricks, so they conduct operations in units of two divisions, and at the same time construct fortifications at key points for defense, leaving the bandits no opportunity to exploit. Furthermore, the bandits' plan is to roam and harass the so-called Red areas of Yongfeng, Xingguo, Yudu, Ruijin, Huichang, and Ningdu. Therefore, their main forces, such as the pseudo-Third Army and even the pseudo-Twelfth Army, remain in the mountains along the border of the four counties of Yu, Xing, Ning, and Yong, using the treacherous mountain terrain as protection. However, the original anti-Red Army air force squadrons, the third and fifth, remain in the province; now the first squadron has also arrived in Jiangxi, with more than twenty fighter planes and more than ten reconnaissance and transport planes. They fly over the bandit areas daily for reconnaissance and bombing, forcing the bandits to hide in forests and caves to avoid their attacks. However, prolonged hiding in the mountains has cut off their supplies, leading to some fleeing and surrendering to the local National Army. The Headquarters has newly established four measures for receiving captured bandits, ordering all units to comply: (1) Reception and placement, (2) Reform through education and training, (3) Implementation of public works, (4) Attacking cities. Commander-in-Chief Chiang also telegraphed all armies, requiring strict examination of captured bandits. Those who capture the bandit leaders Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and Huang Gonglue alive will receive an additional reward of 50,000 yuan, in addition to the original reward of 50,000 yuan. Anyone in the bandit ranks who reports or identifies these leaders, leading to their capture, will be pardoned and heavily rewarded. Furthermore, according to frontline reconnaissance reports received by the Headquarters, the bandits' pseudo-Central Committee and Military Affairs Commission are both located at Bailu Xu, south of Xingguo, guarded by over 3,000 Peng bandits. After receiving this report, the Headquarters also telegraphed Chiang Guangnai, Cai Tingkai, Chiang Dingwen in Xingguo, and Sun Lianzhong's units in Gulonggang, ordering them to jointly encircle and suppress the bandits, and dispatched multiple aircraft to bomb them, aiming to annihilate the bandits and prevent them from fleeing. (August 24)

Demonstration by Russian Naval and Air Forces: Account 74

Shelling at Sanjiang Estuary and Following Our Merchant Ships

Reason: Direct Export of Grain

Harbin Dispatch: From August 18th to 22nd, the Soviet Russian naval and air forces suddenly stationed outside the Sanjiang Estuary for five days, causing great shock along the Songhua River ports. River steamers heading to distant ports like Heihe and Hulin mostly suspended navigation. Only yesterday did this atmosphere of terror begin to dissipate. Seeing that there was little danger ahead, merchant ships resumed their long voyages. The arrival of Russian warships at the Sanjiang Estuary occurred on the night of the 18th. On the morning of the 19th, the merchant ship "Ping An" returned from Hulin to the Songhua River and was intercepted by Russian warships outside the Sanjiang Estuary. It was searched in the middle of the river for an hour before being released. The ship returned and reported to the Jiangfang Marine Corps, learning that fourteen Russian warships were anchored at Xu'ergu on the Russian side and in the Feijiang waterway outside the Sanjiang Estuary. Six aircraft were also stationed along the riverbank at Xu'ergu. On the morning of the 20th, Russian aircraft took off and flew over the border of Fuyuan County, circling our border. The warships fired live ammunition, conducting exercises at the confluence of the three rivers. The sound of cannons boomed, and the roar of airplanes terrified the border residents, reminiscent of the catastrophe of the 18th year (of the Republic), causing widespread panic. Unsure of the Russian intentions, the customs office and the Jiangfang Marine Corps urgently telegraphed Qiqihar for instructions, and advised the Northeast Navigation Bureau not to dispatch long-distance vessels. Passenger ships scheduled to depart for Heihe and Hulin on the 20th were all suspended. On the 21st, telegraph communications between Hulin and Tongjiang were suddenly cut off, further alarming Harbin. The Jiangfang fleet dispatched the warship "Lisui" to Tongjiang for reconnaissance. On the 22nd, the warships "Jiangqing" and "Jiangtong" were ordered to sail to Fujin to provide reassurance. Government and merchant ships shortened their routes that day, only sailing to Fujin. On the evening of the 21st, a portion of the Russian fleet sailed towards Boli. On the 22nd, the "Jiangqing" and "Jiangtong" also arrived in Fujin, and public sentiment gradually calmed. Unexpectedly, early in the morning, the Russian fleet returned towards Boli. Coincidentally, the ships "Fujin" and "Tongshan" arrived at the Sanjiang Estuary simultaneously from Heihe and Hulin. A portion of the Russian fleet and aircraft headed towards Heihe, and upon seeing our merchant ships, followed closely behind in a demonstration of force, only turning back after the two ships entered our river mouth. The "Lisui" sent a telegram after arriving in Tongjiang on the 22nd, stating that the Russian naval and air forces were merely conducting a demonstration and that there were no unexpected incidents. Upon receiving this news, Harbin merchants were reassured, and Shanghai-bound ships of the Northeast Navigation Bureau also resumed sailing. Merchant ships on the Heihe route also resumed their long voyages yesterday and today. Although a portion of the Russian fleet remains at Xu'ergu, they are not taking any action. According to intelligence reports from military authorities, the reason for the arrival of the Russian fleet and aircraft is that the Russian Grain and Stone Trading Company has been purchasing grain in the Fujin area for direct export, which Harbin merchants strongly oppose. Russia fears that our authorities will issue an order prohibiting direct exports, and therefore staged a demonstration as a preliminary act of intimidation. (August 24)

Russia Purchases Grain for Export in Fujin 75

Zhong Yu Reports Significant Losses to the Authorities

Tax Losses Alone Estimated at Four Million

Merchant Losses Not Yet Included

Harbin Dispatch: This year, the markets in Fujin and Wei Chuan in the lower reaches of the Songhua River are depressed. There is a surplus of soybeans and miscellaneous grains produced there.

The Russian state-owned trading company established the Soviet Russian Grain and Stone Trading Office in Harbin, with a branch in Fujin, and contacted local merchants to purchase soybeans and miscellaneous grains at high prices. After the Chamber of Commerce forwarded the request to the Jilin Provincial Government, the province approved it without investigation, and also eliminated the 1.5% export tax to avoid losses to the national treasury. This matter had been brewing since early spring, and by the beginning of this month, the first batch of 2 million "fu" (each "fu" being 30 catties) of grain purchased by the Russians had been realized. They hired nineteen sailboats to transport 60,000 "fu" to Xu'ergu in Russian territory outside the Sanjiang Estuary, where it was handed over to the Russian side. The Russian side then transported it by steamboat to Boli, reloaded it onto trains to Vladivostok, and then shipped it by steamboat to ports in Europe, America, and Southeast Asia for sale. Grain-producing areas along the river flocked to Fujin to sell their grain because the Russians intended to purchase 10 million "fu" and offered high prices. In the past, grain produced along the river was transported to Harbin and then distributed domestically and internationally. The economic center of Harbin relied on the distribution of local products from the lower reaches to maintain its prosperity. Since Russia implemented the export of grain, Harbin's commerce has suffered a sharp decline. Various organizations, concerned about the prosperity of the entire city, repeatedly held meetings and petitioned the government to prohibit it and abolish the export tax system. The two Chambers of Commerce listed several points, hoping to attract the attention of the Northeast government. The most important points were: (1) Because of its location in the lower reaches, Russia can freely send ships into our inland rivers. Fujin is not a commercial port, and Russia's ideology is different from ours. This is like opening the door to let in thieves. Not only can Russian goods be dumped into our country at any time, but also there is an additional channel for the import of Red ideology. (2) Allowing the Russian side to directly export grain to develop the markets in Fujin and Hua Chuan means that grain will no longer be collected and distributed in Harbin. Public tax revenue will be lost, and commerce will be severely affected. Furthermore, the specialty products of northern Manchuria are in danger of being manipulated by Russia in the future. After the Northeast Political Affairs Committee became aware of the benefits and drawbacks of this petition, it ordered the Special District Administrative Chief Executive Office to conduct a thorough investigation, and also ordered the Harbin negotiator to investigate the details. The Special Chief Executive Office has already submitted a report listing the losses suffered by public welfare donations and taxes from direct shipment of goods. Zhong Yu also submitted a special report on Russia's transportation of grain in the lower reaches. The report is as follows:

Cost of export via Harbin: Cost of export via Boli: Losses:

Fujin-Harbin freight: 0.2276 Fujin-Boli freight: 0.2176 0.1476

Customs duty: 0.046 Customs duty: 0.046 0

River donation and waterway donation: 0.0102 River donation and waterway donation: 0.0102 0

Dock donation: 0.027 Dock donation: 0 0.0117

Water police donation: 0.0025 Water police donation: 0.0025 0

Loading charges: 0.0343 Loading charges: 0 0.0343

Thread, sewing mouths, and bags: 0.0075 Thread, mouths, and bags: 0 0.0075

Special police donation: 0.008 Special police donation: 0 0.008

Insurance: 0.003 Insurance: 0.003 0

Harbin-?? freight: 0.2551 0.2551

Autonomy Donation: 0.0225 0.4225

Total: 0.6184 0.7617 0.4867

(The above is the difference per "fu," in yuan. If Russia purchases 10 million "fu" in the lower reaches, the loss in donations and taxes alone will exceed 4 million, not to mention other losses.)

Observing the above table, it is clear that the Jilin Provincial Government's rash approval of Russia's direct purchase of grain and stone for export in the lower reaches has caused great harm. Zhong Yu will travel to Jilin on the 24th to petition the Jilin Provincial Government. However, since the Russian side has already obtained our permission, suddenly canceling it will surely require a great deal of persuasion.

It should be noted that the provinces within the customs are currently suffering from a shortage of grain due to flooding, and are relying on the surplus grain of the Northeast for relief. If the surplus grain of the Northeast is seized by Russia, it will have a huge impact on our people's food supply. Our authorities must take measures to prevent this.

Japanese Warships in Qingdao Send Troops Ashore 76

Members of the Guocui Society Continue to Provoke

Chinese People Not Allowed to Pass Through Japanese Residential Areas

Municipal Steering Committee Sends Letter to City Government Protesting Strongly

Qingdao Dispatch: After the case of Japanese residents in this city murdering Chinese people, City Government Secretary-General Hu Jiafeng and Japanese Consul Hori Koichi met formally at the International Club. Both sides expressed their desire for a peaceful resolution. Our citizens also understood the situation and believed that the matter should be handled by the City Government and that no further incidents should be created, lest complications arise and cause regret. However, the Japanese acted differently, still seeking trouble everywhere, fearing that the incident would not escalate. Members of the Guocui Society continued to patrol the Xiaobao Island area with weapons every day. After 10 PM every night, Chinese people were not allowed to pass through the areas where Japanese people lived, and Chinese people mostly took detours. Last night, a peddler named Zhang mistakenly entered the area where Japanese people lived and was caught by the patrol, resulting in severe beating before being released after a long time. Furthermore, Police Officer Wang of the Sifang Xiaocunzhuang Police Station was patrolling outside last night and was seen by Japanese people. Without asking about the situation, they fired two shots at Wang. Fortunately, he was not hit. The police officer immediately returned to the station to report the incident to the headquarters for investigation. The Japanese warship "Kuma" organized a patrol team from its marine corps, all fully armed. Without notifying the municipal authorities, they secretly landed on the 24th evening and hid inside the Japanese Resident Group. They patrolled along Liaocheng Road and Liaoning Road every night, ostensibly to "protect" the overseas Chinese, but the real intention is unknown. Furthermore, the Qingdao Xinbao, a newspaper run by Japanese residents in this city, not only fabricated rumors and conducted counter-propaganda regarding this case, but also published an editorial on the 26th of this month entitled "Japanese Residents Should Advocate Proposing to the League of Nations to Return the Lease of Qingdao." The arguments made in the editorial directly disregarded our national sovereignty and provoked animosity among our people. It is reported that the City Government has lodged a strong protest with the Japanese Consulate. The Municipal Steering Committee believes that the incident of Japanese residents murdering Chinese people was an organized and planned riot, and the evidence is solid and undeniable. However, after the incident, the Japanese side falsely accused the Chinese side of being instigated by the Municipal Party Department behind the scenes, creating misleading counter-propaganda in an attempt to shirk responsibility. Therefore, yesterday, they also sent a letter to the City Government requesting that a strong protest be lodged with the Japanese side. (August 27)

Aviation Administration Expands Air Force 77

Newly Purchased Fighter and Bomber Aircraft Arrive in Nanjing

To strengthen its aviation capabilities, the Aviation Administration ordered six fighter aircraft from Germany and twenty bomber aircraft from the United States, which have been shipped to Shanghai. The six fighter aircraft were manufactured by the German Junkers Company, each costing 150,000 Chinese dollars, with 540 horsepower, capable of traveling over 200 miles per hour. The fuselage is entirely oil-painted in bluish-gray. The German instructor Xue Te, who is organizing the fighter squadron for the Aviation Administration, has begun flying and conducting fighter training. The twenty bomber aircraft were manufactured by the American Curtiss Aircraft Factory, each costing 130,000 Chinese dollars, with over 400 horsepower, capable of flying over 180 miles per hour. The fuselage is painted green with a red tail. They have been distributed to the seven squadrons under the Aviation Administration, with three or two aircraft assigned to each squadron. Each squadron will first send pilots to Shanghai for test flights. After they are proficient, they will come to Nanjing. Among them, the three aircraft assigned to the Seventh Air Squadron have already flown to the front lines to join the suppression of the Red bandits. The rest are still training in Nanjing. The aircraft soaring in the clouds these days are these aircraft undergoing test flights. According to Shui Qirui, a pilot of the Seventh Air Squadron, the Aviation Administration has a total of seven squadrons, with twenty-one sub-squadrons. It is now planning to expand them into seven major squadrons, each squadron divided into three companies, each company divided into three sub-squadrons, following the Japanese aviation organization system, and hopes to achieve this in the shortest possible time.

The "Guangsheng" Steamship from Shanghai to Shantou 78

Sinks Near Fuying Island 79

Over Two Hundred Passengers and Crew Perish Together

Shantou Dispatch: The "Guangsheng" Steamship, which regularly travels between Shanghai and Hong Kong, departed from Shanghai on the 8th. On the way, it encountered a storm and sank near Fuying Island, sixty miles north of Fuzhou Prefecture. According to Jardine Matheson & Co.'s report, the "Guangsheng" Steamship carried a heavy load of soybean cakes, soybean oil, miscellaneous grains, miscellaneous goods, etc. when it departed from Shanghai. It had six Western crew members, fifty-six Chinese crew members, and over two hundred passengers. It departed Shanghai on the 8th and was scheduled to arrive in Shantou on the 11th. When it reached the vicinity of Wenzhou, it suddenly received a distress call from the "Weisheng" Steamship. The "Guangsheng" Steamship broke down and went missing. Who knew that the "Weisheng" ran aground at Nanguan Bay, but fortunately was unharmed, while the "Guangsheng" Steamship disappeared without a trace. The Jardine Matheson & Co. agent in Shantou and Shanghai sent the "Zesheng," "Hesheng," and "Fusheng" to search. On the evening of the 21st, the "Fusheng" reported discovering traces of a shipwreck near Fuying Island, sixty miles north of Fuzhou, with thick soybean oil covering the waves on the sea surface. Fishermen also picked up a Jardine Matheson & Co. lifebuoy and rescued four Chinese and Western male corpses. In Fuying Bay, they rescued a Westerner who was tightly holding a Jardine Matheson & Co. lifebuoy. Due to being in the water for too long and being battered by the waves, he was barely breathing and unable to speak. He was transported to Fu'ning Prefecture for medical treatment. The details of the "Guangsheng" Steamship's sinking will only be known after this person is able to speak. According to the "Fusheng" Steamship's report, the Jardine Matheson & Co. employee's account, and various information obtained by the customs, it is believed that the "Guangsheng" Steamship has indeed sunk, and the location of the accident is within one mile of Fuying Island. The Shantou Post Office issued a notice yesterday stating that thirty-nine bags of mail and one hundred bags of parcels sent to Shantou on the ship, as well as letters from various places transferred from Shanghai to Shantou eight days ago, and two bags of letters from Seattle, USA, and letters from London, England, via Siberia, have not been received by the post office. It is said that the "Guangsheng" Steamship was a merchant ship of the British Jardine Matheson & Co., traveling to ports such as Hong Kong, Shantou, Shanghai, and Qingdao. The ship was 290 feet long, 42 feet wide, and 15 feet deep, built in Glasgow, England in 1902. The owner was a British man named Henry, the first mate was Mr. Bi, the second mate was Mr. Li, and there were four British chief and assistant engineers, as well as fifty-nine Chinese sailors and crew members. The ship had a capacity of 2,283 tons. This time, the entire ship sank. Among the passengers and crew of over two hundred people, apart from this Westerner, at most two or three others were rescued. The loss of cargo is estimated to be over 300,000, which is also a tragedy. (August 22)

Puyi's Concubine Proposes Divorce 80

Intolerable Abuse After Nine Years of Marriage

Concubine's Sister Plans Escape from the Palace

Eastern Palace Urges Puyi to be Open-Minded

Divorce Expected to be the Outcome

Tianjin Dispatch: The deposed Emperor Puyi married in December of the 11th year of the Republic (1922), taking one Empress and one Concubine. In the 13th year of the Republic (1924), he was expelled from the Forbidden City in Beijing and hid in the Japanese Legation in the Dongjiaominxiang. The following year, he took refuge in the Japanese Concession in Tianjin, first living in Zhang Garden and then purchasing Wu Guangxin's residence. His Empress and Concubine followed him. The Concubine, named Wenxiu, was seventeen years old when she married and is now twenty-five, meaning she has been married for nine years. Recently, due to intolerable abuse, she planned an escape and hired a lawyer to protect her rights. The details are as follows: According to the Concubine, in the past nine years in Puyi's household, she has had absolutely no freedom of movement and has suffered abuse. First, the Empress did not allow her to be close to Puyi, cutting off the joy of life and leaving no marital affection. Second, the eunuchs were overbearing and she had to be at their beck and call. One eunuch even said that the Emperor had no kindness towards her and that she should die quickly and that if the Emperor ordered her to die, she could not disobey. Under this kind of pressure, she felt it was unbearable. Her only remaining relative was her sister, Wen Shan, who was the daughter-in-law of a certain Second Master, namely the daughter-in-law of Old Prince Qing. In recent years, the Concubine has repeatedly considered suicide. Her sister often visited and comforted her with words of encouragement. Recently, the Concubine was forced too far by the eunuchs and took the opportunity to stab her throat with scissors to commit suicide, but she was rescued. However, since then, her sadness has intensified. The eunuchs asked the Concubine's sister to enter the palace to persuade her. Since then, the Concubine's sister has been able to enter and leave the palace with relative freedom. Yesterday (the 25th) at 3 PM, the Concubine's sister explained to Puyi and the Empress that her sister was crying day and night and took her out for a walk to relax. They took a eunuch and sat in a car. They went to the National Hotel and entered a certain room. The Concubine's sister suddenly said to the eunuch, "You go back first. The Concubine will stay here and will sue the Emperor in court." The eunuch was shocked upon hearing this. The Concubine's sister handed him a letter, saying, "This matter has nothing to do with you. You can take this letter back to the Emperor." The three lawyers that the Concubine had hired in advance also entered from outside the door. The eunuch could only retreat. The letter was written by the lawyers and requested that Puyi send a representative to formally negotiate with the lawyers. After the eunuch left, Puyi and the Concubine expressed their deep affection for each other and that there was no abuse and asked people not to misunderstand. The lawyers said that the matter has already reached this point and that the Concubine is determined not to return. If Puyi wants to reconcile, he should immediately acknowledge her complete freedom, otherwise there is no other option but to file a lawsuit in court. Last night, Puyi convened an imperial conference to discuss how to deal with the matter. Since the Concubine and her sister had left the hotel through the back door after the eunuch left, they found another safe place. (August 26)

Further report: After Puyi heard that his Concubine had escaped from the palace, he became very anxious. He immediately notified his permanent lawyer to contact the Concubine's lawyers and sent staff to search for the Concubine everywhere. The situation was extremely tense all night, even to the point of searching the residence of a certain Second Master. The Second Master happened to be away in Pan and had not returned. The Second Master's wife told the people who came that they were looking for the Concubine there and she was still looking for her daughter-in-law. After searching everywhere with no trace, Puyi's heart finally died. He also knew that the situation could not be reversed. According to the rules of the ancestors, the concubine should not stay away from the palace at night. The demands of the Concubine's representatives were very pressing. If he allowed her to sue, he would certainly lose. Therefore, since yesterday (August 26) morning, his attitude changed drastically, hoping that the matter would be resolved peacefully and that everything could be done as she wished. Therefore, the lawyers of both parties agreed to hold the first meeting at 6 PM yesterday to formally discuss divorce procedures. It is said that the content is not difficult to negotiate. However, the Concubine's side requested a large amount of alimony, and Puyi's side requested that there be no public statement after the settlement. These two points may be disputed. In short, the outcome of this case will definitely be a happy divorce. The meeting was held in great secrecy. It was easier to detect bandits, but it was heard that the proposed plan had been reported to Puyi by the male lawyer that night. It will only be considered final after Puyi has discussed it with the ministers. It was also heard that after the Concubine left the palace, the Empress of the Eastern Palace strongly urged the Emperor to respect humanitarianism and not to pursue the matter too much. Puyi's open-mindedness was due to the Empress's words. (August 27)

Wang Rongbao Investigates 81

The Wanxian Incident Report (Continued) 82

On July 3rd, at 2:00 AM, dozens of Koreans in Incheon's outer district threw stones at Chinese barber shops and restaurants, breaking glass and light bulbs. By dawn, rumors of a Korean riot intensified, and overseas Chinese residents flocked to the Chinese quarter for refuge. At 8:00 AM, Director Jiang of the Incheon branch office went to the police station to negotiate a cessation, and simultaneously reported to the Consulate General. At 8:00 PM that evening, Koreans suddenly gathered a crowd of approximately three thousand people, launching a major riot that plunged the entire city into chaos. Overseas Chinese men and women all fled for safety. The doors and windows of Chinese businesses were smashed by the Koreans, and the police were unable to stop them. Director Jiang and Chairman Fu of the Chamber of Commerce went to the police station, requesting that the police be armed and dispatched. The police chief declined, stating that he had not received orders from the provincial office, so he was unable to comply. Later, the rioters regrouped and advanced towards the Chinese quarter. Fortunately, the overseas Chinese jointly defended it, preventing entry. They then retreated, throwing stones at Chinese shops along the way and engaging in scattered looting. Although many overseas Chinese were injured that night, there were no deaths. Major Chinese businesses did not sustain significant losses. Though the rioters dispersed by dawn, the atmosphere remained tense. The Incheon office telephoned the Consulate General, requesting the Governor-General's office to send additional armed police. Simultaneously, they went to the police station for questioning. In the afternoon, Consul General Zhang arrived in Incheon for inspection and negotiated with the police station. The police chief claimed full responsibility. When Consul General Zhang returned to the capital, around 9:00 PM, it was reported that Koreans were again gathering crowds by beating gongs in the outer district, amassing around five thousand people. Wielding wooden sticks, iron bars, knives, and axes, they searched everywhere, smashing and destroying. All Chinese businesses in both the inner and outer districts were targeted. The rioters used merchandise to smash open doors, then shattered them with axes, cut telephone and electric wires, looted and tore up goods, and discarded them on the streets. Finally, they tied bolts of cloth and silk to tree trunks or wrapped them around utility poles. The police were powerless to protect them. The branch office, upon receiving the report, urgently telegraphed Consul General Zhang to negotiate with the Governor-General's office, as there were no large troops of soldiers and police to come to Incheon to assist. At the same time, it telegraphed the Incheon police station, urging them to earnestly protect the lives and property of all overseas Chinese in the city. At 3:00 AM on the 5th, seventeen armed police officers and military police from the capital arrived. The police were also armed. Seeing the unfavorable situation, they fired two shots into the air, and the rioters began to retreat. The Chinese quarter was heavily guarded, and fortunately, they did not break through. Two overseas Chinese residents were found beaten to death: Lian Kuishan and Li Junji. Two others, Lu Huanxin and Wang Youzhi, were seriously injured and sent to the hospital for treatment. Simultaneously, cargo trucks were urgently hired to transport overseas Chinese from near and far to the Chinese quarter for refuge, totaling approximately one thousand five hundred people. More than twenty others sustained minor injuries. On the evening of the 5th, the rioters gathered crowds of thousands around the Chinese quarter, hoping to break in. Fortunately, the police scattered them with cavalry. Fires were then set outside the city, destroying two locations. The branch office and the Chamber of Commerce sheltered approximately three thousand six hundred overseas Chinese. Starting from the 6th, the situation gradually calmed down, and overseas Chinese residents boarded the Chinese-owned "Litong" steamship and the Japanese-owned "Kyodo Maru" to return to their home country, reaching eight thousand people. The direct losses to overseas Chinese in this incident are estimated at around ninety thousand Japanese yen, and indirect losses are still being investigated in detail.

The Korean riot in Seoul occurred around 10:00 PM on July 3rd. Korean residents threw stones at many overseas Chinese businesses, destroying doors, windows, and glass. Any Chinese encountered on the streets were beaten. The Consulate General immediately telephoned the military police and various police stations to rigorously suppress and protect. Before dawn on the 4th, overseas Chinese merchants, farmers, and laborers from inside and outside Seoul flocked to the consulate to report that the riots were intensifying and the damage was already considerable. Consul General Zhang repeatedly went to the Governor-General's office to request the swift dispatch of armed troops and police for protection. Simultaneously, he notified various consulate branches. The Chinese Chamber of Commerce and representatives of various organizations visited various government agencies and newspaper offices, urging them to ease tensions between the Chinese and Koreans. The Consul General also sent a letter to the Korean Administrative Superintendent-General, requesting that he quickly devise a comprehensive protection plan and judiciously dispatch armed troops and police. By that time, over a thousand overseas Chinese had come to the consulate for refuge. On the morning of the 5th, refugees continued to arrive in an endless stream. That day, Sunday, the Consulate General once again presented four emergency measures to the Governor-General's office. Subsequently, a telephone response stated that Chinese residents in remote areas inside and outside Seoul could be escorted to the Consulate General for temporary refuge by the police stations. The police in each province had been ordered to be fully vigilant. Areas with a higher concentration of Chinese residents in Seoul had been instructed to provide on-site protection. The Consulate General immediately notified the Chinese Chamber of Commerce to dispatch automobiles to Longshan, Mapo, and other locations to transport Chinese residents to the consulate. On that day, the number of overseas Chinese seeking refuge was estimated to be over two thousand. On the 6th, Consul General Zhang visited the Police Bureau Chief of the Governor-General's office, requesting that he order all provinces to dispatch additional armed troops and police to suppress and control the situation. Subsequently, the Bureau Chief came to the consulate and replied that he had strictly ordered police in all provinces to be on alert. On that day, approximately three thousand six hundred overseas Chinese residents arrived at the consulate for refuge. On the 7th, various police stations dispatched police to escort more overseas Chinese residents to the consulate. As of that day, the total number, before and after, reached three thousand six or seven hundred people. On the 7th, 8th, and 9th, Zhang continued to negotiate and question the Governor-General's office. Riots in various places were still continuing. According to reports, the homes and properties of over sixty overseas Chinese families, including Xu Xiuyi and others, were destroyed. Approximately one hundred forty overseas Chinese residents, including Niu Ji and others, were injured or beaten. Over two hundred forty people, including Sun Junji and others, suffered property losses. According to the aforementioned report, the extent of losses and injuries suffered by overseas Chinese residents inside and outside Seoul was extremely severe. The accurate figures are still being investigated in detail. (To be continued)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 83

County Government Convenes Disaster Relief Meeting: This year, Wuhan and other areas have experienced flooding, and Gaobao and other areas in northern Jiangsu province have also suffered disastrous levee breaches, resulting in the drowning of hundreds of thousands of people. Yesterday, during the preparatory meeting for the Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, this matter was discussed. It was deemed necessary to establish a disaster relief association. The county government was appointed as the convener, and a meeting was scheduled for 1:00 PM on the 31st of this month to discuss fundraising and relief methods. The county government has already notified the leaders of various organizations and local gentry.

Patrol Captains Surround District Head Demanding Salary: The city and township housing police levy is collected by the district office to pay the salaries of the police in the four districts, with the county Public Security Bureau providing supplementary funding and investigation expenses. However, revenue falls short of expenditure, and the office is already in arrears of nearly two thousand gold dollars. Consequently, the payment of police salaries has occasionally been delayed by a few days due to fundraising difficulties. Today (the 29th), the patrol captains of the four city and township districts, demanding their July salaries, gathered at the county Public Security Bureau and summoned District Head Zhong, surrounding him and demanding their pay, with many accusations. The matter remained unresolved. It is reported that District Head Zhong, feeling pressured and humiliated by the crowd, immediately prepared a statement of accounts, clarifying the district office's arrears. He has submitted this statement to County Magistrate Shen, requesting his intervention, and has also proposed removing the housing police levy to avoid resentment.

Seawall Damage After Hurricane: The Jinshanzui seawall in this county suffered damage. On the night of the 25th of this month, a sudden hurricane arose, accompanied by torrential rain. The tide surged violently, overflowing the seawall. Giant rocks weighing thousands of pounds were blown onto the seawall surface. The intensity of the storm was unprecedented. The next day, the storm finally subsided. Inspection revealed that from the first section of Xitang to the twelfth section, 1,889 key piles had been washed away. The earthen sections had been eroded by two to three feet in various places. Stone blocks from the stone surface and slope were blown onto the seawall surface. The top beam and wall panels of the third section's cement project were also washed away. East of the Second Seawall, the outer tidal flat, spanning five to six li, where salt-making residents lived, and numerous ash fields were completely destroyed. The earthwork at the North and South Pier was eroded, leaving only a few feet remaining. The tide flowed over the seawall like a torrent. Fortunately, the patrol office supervised rescue efforts, preventing a breach. However, the authorities still need to take extra precautions to avoid the danger of an autumn flood.

Major Bandit Lu Yaosheng and Others Escorted to Songjiang: Bandit leader Lu Yaosheng, a subordinate of Tai Bao Ashu, and Yang Azhao, were arrested in Fengxian County. Today, the Fengxian County government dispatched police to escort the two criminals, Lu and Yang, to the Songjiang Pacification Sub-district Headquarters for interrogation.

Fengxian 84

Lu Yaosheng Requests Execution: Jiangzhe major bandit Lu Yaosheng, apprehended by the county police force, has been interrogated six times by County Magistrate Shen Qingchen and Investigator Xu Cheng, and has confessed without denial. During the last interrogation last night, the bandit confessed to having committed robbery for twenty years, and his crimes were long known. He only asked for a public execution to end his sinful life. As for Yang Meimei (the woman he kidnapped and raped), he requested that the court send her back to her parents' home, so that he could die in peace, revealing a lingering sense of regret. Regarding the cause of his arrest, he claimed that since his gang was defeated and dispersed last year, he and Chen Qunlin had been engaged in fishing off the coast of Fengxian, and had robbed two sand boats to make a floating home. He intended to hide in the desolate滩, protecting his remaining life. Unexpectedly, Chen kidnapped a hostage in Nanhui and fled first in breach of trust, leaving him with nowhere to live. He had no choice but to temporarily take refuge in Chen Guanlin's home (where he was arrested). He had planned to take Yang Meimei to Ningbo the next morning and make other plans. Now, he was suddenly arrested, perhaps by fate. County Magistrate Shen believes that the bandit's crimes are punishable by execution under the law for punishing bandits, but it is unclear whether the authority to make this decision rests with the county, so he has sent a telegram to the province for approval.

County Government Reports Disaster and Stores Grain: The county government is currently reporting the severity of the wind disaster and the failure of the autumn harvest, based on reports from various district offices. Today, it telegraphed the provincial government, requesting that officials be sent for inspection. On the one hand, the county government meeting ordered the Food Committee to purchase and store grain as soon as possible. It also invited local gentry and wealthy individuals, Chen Huazhou, Song (blank), Shen Menglian, and Cheng Weiyu, to organize a Food Maintenance Association, intending to raise funds and purchase 10,000 dan of rice in the shortest possible time to meet urgent needs.

Suzhou 85

Police and Bandits Exchange Fire, Hostages Rescued: In the area of Huamubin, Xigang, Wujiang County, over ten bandits arrived at the home of villager Li Longsheng on the 21st of this month and kidnapped Li Longsheng's sons, Li Shunlin, Li Shunshan, and Li Aqi, all three missing. On the 28th, Captain Xu of the 14th Wujiang Water Police Squad learned that the bandits were hiding the hostages on a boat in the Xinkai Road area, waiting for ransom. Captain Xu immediately led a detachment to suppress them. That night, they encountered three bandit boats with over twenty bandits. The two sides exchanged fire for a short time, sinking one bandit boat and rescuing the three hostages. The bandits fled to the northwest.

Fundraising by Borrowing and Collecting Rent: The Finance Bureau of the Wu County government received repeated orders from the provincial government to raise 200,000 yuan in construction public bonds. Yesterday (the 29th), it convened a meeting of bond-raising committee members and local figures to discuss fundraising methods. As a result, due to the difficulty of fundraising, it was decided to borrow and collect one month's rent from shop owners. Those with less than ten months of rent due would be exempt. Starting in September, the rent would be collected evenly over four months. The Finance Bureau would issue receipts, which could be exchanged for bonds. This rent would be borne by the landlords and would be used to aid flood victims in various townships in Wu County, with half of it retained by the provincial government.

Wuxi 86

Shocking News of Filial Son Killing Father: Chen Genda, a 60-year-old resident of Qiujiutu Chenjia Alley, Duomen, 16th District (Wan'an City) of this county, has always been engaged in farming. He has over ten mu of fertile land and two oxen. He is married to a woman surnamed (blank) and has two sons, Chunquan and Rongquan, both of whom are married. The brothers live separately. At the time, it was stated that the father, Genda, would be supported by the eldest son, Chunquan. However, Chunquan is inherently violent, so he often fought with his father. The day before yesterday evening, Chen Genda traveled far from home, and by the time he returned, Chunquan had already eaten dinner. Genda informed his second son, Rongquan, of the situation. Chunquan overheard this and became enraged. He rushed to Rongquan's home, verbally abused his father, and struck Genda on the head with his opium pipe, shattering his skull. Genda fell to the ground, bleeding profusely and barely breathing. Neighbors bandaged the wound, but Genda was old and lost too much blood. He died of his injuries yesterday. Chunquan, seeing that he had caused a disaster, said to his younger brother Rongquan, "I have killed our father. I will bear all funeral expenses. You will be responsible for the funeral expenses when our mother passes away." Rongquan, fearing his fierceness, did not argue with him and allowed him to hastily arrange the funeral.

Hiring Small Steamers to Rescue Flood Victims in Northern Jiangsu: This year, continuous rain has caused disasters across the country. News of the breach of Hongze Lake in Jiangsu province has also arrived. The dikes have collapsed, turning the area into a vast ocean. Residents in counties near the lake in northern Jiangsu have lost all their homes and property. Old and young alike are struggling in the water, displaced and destitute. The provincial government meeting decided to prepare measures for disaster relief, ordering counties in southern Jiangsu to collect steamers to go and rescue them. Xu Jigui, director of the local Public Security Bureau, upon receiving the order, immediately invited Mao Feng, director of the Construction Bureau, to consult with Chairman Qian Sunqing of the County Chamber of Commerce. He also summoned representatives of the Steamer Association to the meeting for discussion. As a result, the Steamer Association ordered four companies, including Licheng and Xinjiang, to allocate four steamers and attached tugboats. Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, they reported to the Public Security Bureau and set off for the disaster area in northern Jiangsu to rescue flood victims.

Changzhou 87

Requisitioning Steamers for Disaster Relief: On the 28th, the Wujin County government received a telegram from the province stating that the Canal dikes in northern Jiangsu had collapsed and flood victims were in urgent need of rescue. They were ordered to requisition steamers and tugboats and send personnel to Zhenjiang to await dispatch. The Xinjing and Gu Xinjiang steamers were requisitioned, as well as four civilian boats. That night, Patrol Officer Zhao Yiji was dispatched with police escort to Zhenjiang to await orders.

Fourth District Embankments Breached: The river embankments along the Wolong Township, Fourth District of Wujin County, were completely breached the day before yesterday. The entire continent became a swamp, with houses collapsing, livestock drowning, and people struggling in the water. In addition to taking measures to rescue them, on the 28th, District Head Liu Baorun sent a telegram to the county government requesting inspection.

Nantong 88

Severe Coastal Tide Disaster: In various ports along the river in Nantong, including Yao and Ren, on the 26th, the river tide rose sharply, breaching the dikes in six places, each breach exceeding ten zhang. The tide poured in, flooding houses, fields, and crops, causing a terrible disaster. On the 27th, the water receded slightly, and the county government ordered the Construction Bureau to rush the emergency repair work. Currently, the Cheng Yao Road is blocked by water, and incoming and outgoing mail cannot be transported. The county government, considering the severity of the disaster, specially convened a meeting of the business community to discuss relief and post-disaster measures.

Qingjiang 89

County Government Detains Gate Official: The Huaiyin County government recently received a letter from the Huai-Pi Embankment Works Office requesting the detention of Zhao Yucheng, the Qing'an Floodgate official and concurrently manager of the Shuangjin Floodgate, to urge the opening of the floodgate. The county government immediately ordered the police to arrest him. However, the gate official Zhao had already fled. According to the police report to the county, residents near the Shuangjin Floodgate stated that after Zhao was summoned by the commander-in-chief of the 25th Route Army during the high water period, he disappeared. Even his family members are unaware of his whereabouts. After receiving the report, the county government, in addition to first sending a letter to the Works Office and inquiring about how this case should be handled, also ordered the police to continue the arrest.

Hangzhou 90

Large Quantity of Red Pill Case Criminals Escorted to Hangzhou: In the case where 400,000 red pills were seized by anti-Japanese association inspectors at the Nanshingiao Station in Hangzhou City on the 2nd of this month, the consignee Hong Peiwen and Shen Qing, the manager of the Shin Da Transport Company's Nanshingiao Station who transported the red pills, were both deemed to be highly suspicious after being interrogated by the court. Both were arrested and visitation was suspended. It is now reported that Li Chucai, the sender from Shanghai, has also been apprehended. He was escorted to Hangzhou yesterday, interrogated by the criminal court prosecutor, and sent to the detention center for strict punishment.

Xiaoshan 91

Typhoon and Rainstorm Kill People: Since the 25th and 26th, when Xiaoshan suffered a major wind and rain disaster, the loss of crops and cotton in the four townships is incalculable. It is now known that walls have collapsed, awnings have been overturned, and glass and tiles have been blown off and broken along the streets in the urban area. The Wushen Temple at Zhang Pan Bridge outside the South Gate overturned, crushing two men and women to death. The walls of the Xianjia Xu family collapsed, crushing an old woman. The house of the Yintou Dai family collapsed, crushing a seven-year-old child to death. Five houses collapsed at the Zengjia Bridge outside the East Gate, crushing a father and son to death. A large camphor tree in Huchen of the West Township was uprooted, destroying a house and injuring two people. The tragic situation is difficult to describe in detail.

Theatrical Troupe Trouble Caused by Soldiers: The Xiaoshan County Health Committee held a theatrical performance at the Huoshen Temple in the urban area to raise funds. Unexpectedly, several conscription officers from the military garrisoned in Xiaoshan, because they did not have tickets to see the play, were kindly advised by Fu Konglun, the director of the venue, to purchase tickets. The soldiers then smashed property and injured an elderly woman surnamed Zhang and Xia patrol head. The main culprit, Wang Zhirui, is still at large. It is still unknown how to resolve this case of injury and destruction.

Ningbo 92

Chang Yu Electrocuted While Fishing: Dai Jiafa, a Shaoxing resident who lives outside the West Gate, is in his forties and earns his living by fishing. The city experienced a hurricane on the 25th. The salt tide flooded all the fishing ponds, and big fish were scurrying around. Dai was fishing in the rain, but there was an electricity pole in that location. The lead wire was blown off by the hurricane. Dai picked it up, and was electrocuted and fell into the river. He died.

Hefei 93

Bandit Leader Who Shot His Way Out of A Robbery: The home of Liu Zhonglian in Liujia Village, Linhe River, was suddenly visited the day before yesterday by a guest who claimed to be surnamed Chen, carrying two gift packages. Liu came out to see him, but did not recognize him. As Liu was wondering, the guest opened the package and pulled out a pistol, demanding 500 yuan. Liu knew he had encountered a robber and searched all his belongings, obtaining 160 yuan. The bandit then wrote a note demanding 140 yuan in three days, and 200 yuan three days after that. The bandit was satisfied and asked for wine and food before leaving. Three days later, he personally came to Liu's house to collect the money. Three days after that, in Changlinhe Town, he summoned Liu to hand over the money. Liu then reported to Chief Ding Rui Ting, who led a team to arrest the bandit at the Ding Tea House. During interrogation, the bandit's real name was revealed to be Fei Guangnian, 22 years old. The team escorted him to the county. When they reached the Huoyan Field, a large group of bandits came to intercept them. Chief Ding fired at the bandits while at the same time shooting Fei dead. By evening, the bandits were driven away.
