Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces - Yesterday's Report 96

The following is a report on the situation yesterday regarding disaster relief for the floods in Jiangbei and other provinces:

Jiangsu Charity Relief Association: Minutes of the Second Standing Committee Meeting

The Jiangsu Charity Relief Association held its second standing committee meeting at the Renji Hall on Six Malu at 5:00 PM yesterday.

Attendees

Committee members Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Shi Liangcai, Wen Lanting, Hu Bijiang, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Yinjiang, Huang Hanzhi, Weng Yinchu, Gu Xinyi, Yu Shaoliu, and over twenty others were present. Huang Hanzhi chaired the meeting, and Xiao Zhan Diao served as the recording secretary.

Reported Matters

(1) Fifteen breaches occurred at Gao Shao, resulting in countless deaths and unprecedented devastation. A standing committee member was dispatched to Zhenjiang by night train on the 28th with 20,000 yuan to discuss with relief associates and procure additional ships and dry rations for urgent rescue efforts. (2) 123 disaster reports have been received from various counties. (3) Qiao Mengqian, the special commissioner for surveying the Ningxu area, returned to Zhenjiang Hospital due to illness. Qiu Xiangxian, a relief associate, has been dispatched to survey the Xu area. Wang Shaoyun, head of the document section of this association, has been appointed to replace him to survey Jiangpu County in the Ning area. Zhu Zhongjian, the special commissioner for surveying Gao Bao Xing Tai Dong Yan Fu, Chen Borong, the special commissioner for surveying Huai Lian Si, and Yuan Xiaogu, the special commissioner for surveying Jintan Liyang Jiangdu Yangzhou Zhenjiang Yixing, have all departed separately. Yuan Xiaogu is now reassigned to Gao Shao for urgent rescue. Liu Xin San is hired for the survey in Yixing Jintan. (4) The Longtan Chamber of Commerce reported the collapse of the embankment in a telegram, describing severe devastation. The Qiao commissioner was instructed by telegram to head over there. (5) Cao Songqiao donated four boxes of Niàn Zhèn Pī Lì Dān from Hankou, which have been transferred to the Water Disaster Relief Associations of various provinces and will be transported for distribution immediately. (6) Over the past few days, emergency relief directors have been hired for various counties. Those agreed upon are Qiao Mengqian for Tongshan, Chen Borong for Bao Ying, Zhu Bofu for Lianshui, Zhu Zhongjian for Gaoyou, Yuan Xiaogu for Jiangdu, and Cao Songqiao for Yangzhou. (7) Letters to all fundraising committee members of the Provincial Relief Association have been sent. (8) 418 donation registers have been issued by the Provincial Relief Association. (9) Due to the standing committee member's arrival in Zhenjiang, Yu Shaoliu, a member of the executive committee, is temporarily acting on his behalf in the association's duties. (10) Amount of relief funds handled (11) Amount of relief funds disbursed.

Matters for Discussion

(1) Committee member Wang Yiting proposed that due to the countless deaths and desperate situation caused by the Gao Shao breaches, a discussion on how to assist should be held. The resolution was to accommodate inland disaster victims by transporting them to Shanghai in batches for easier resettlement. In addition to urgent fundraising by this association, a request should be made to the National Government's Disaster Relief Committee for adequate relief. (2) Committee members Huang Hanzhi and Cheng Jinsheng proposed that a telegram should be sent to all parties to call for help in response to the Gao Shao catastrophe, and that a draft telegram be prepared for discussion. The resolution was to approve the original draft with revisions and also to send a telegram to officials in the North requesting their joint assistance in relief efforts. (3) Committee members Wang Yiting and Huang Hanzhi proposed the nomination of Weng Yinchu, Zhu Yinjiang, and Gu Xinyi as economic committee members of the association. The resolution was to approve the proposal. (4) Committee member Cheng Jinsheng proposed that a letter from the Department of Agriculture and Mining requesting 30,000 yuan to protect draft cattle be discussed. The resolution was that saving lives is more urgent and they are unable to address this matter. (5) Committee members Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, and Cheng Jinsheng proposed that a list of counties for which the association plans to provide urgent relief be presented for discussion. The resolution was that in addition to the sixteen counties already designated, including Gaoyou and Baoying, Taixian, Yancheng, and Funing counties will be added. Representatives from Gaoyou, Dong Junde and Ji Xiaozhou, were present at the meeting to report on the dire situation in Gaoyou. The original draft of the telegram is appended below.

Urgent Telegram for Help

To the National Government's Executive Yuan, Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Industry, and Jiangsu Provincial Government: We received a telegram from the Baoying Relief Association at 7:00 PM today stating that several breaches had occurred north of Gaoyou, devastating countless areas, and that transportation between Bao and Gao has been severed. They requested immediate assistance to alleviate the crisis. We were shocked. While we were discussing rescue measures, we also read a telegram from Chairman Zhang Songfu to Chairman Xu Jingren stating that the Grand Canal had breached in fifteen places, submerging Shao Bai and Gaoyou, resulting in countless deaths and no means of escape. Songfu arrived in Yangzhou yesterday and witnessed the devastation, pleading for immediate assistance. We also received a telegram from Superintendent Zhang, reporting that the commander stationed in Yangzhou had reported that Shao Bai was completely submerged and that Gaoyou had also collapsed at 2:00 PM on the same afternoon, submerging the entire city. The loss of population in the vast expanse of water could not be determined. Xinghua and other counties bordering Gaoyou, located at the bottom of the "cauldron," have also suffered. The loss of life and property is incalculable. This unprecedented catastrophe is unbearable. Currently, the afflicted people are calling for help from treetops, with corpses and debris floating downstream. Many others are left to die. Lives hang by a thread. In addition to dispatching personnel with dry rations and hiring boats to provide urgent rescue, this is merely a drop in the bucket and cannot provide universal relief. We request that you send personnel to the disaster areas to provide urgent relief to help the people. We await your orders with utmost urgency. The embankment of the Grand Canal is two zhang higher than the houses of the residents. In the event of a major flood, the counties connected to the rivers and lakes rely on the eastern embankment for protection. If the embankment breaches, the lake water, approximately 100 li wide and 500 li long, will immediately flood the counties east of the embankment, which are below two zhang in height, and all will become fish food. Historically, the nation has attached great importance to river defense plans for this reason. Now, the Grand Canal embankment has breached in more than ten places, and Gao Bao Jiang Xing Tai Dong Yan Fu and other counties will be completely submerged. Although the degree of devastation may vary, it is estimated that the total number of deaths will be no less than 200,000 to 300,000. This overwhelming disaster is unprecedented. Looking north at the disaster area, we cannot help but weep. In addition to quickly organizing rescue efforts, we dare to request that you appoint senior officials to expedite the process of plugging the breaches. At this moment, many people in the disaster area are still on rooftops and trees, waiting for rescue. The cost of accommodating the survivors will be enormous. We also beg you to quickly allocate massive funds to save these people. We submit our plea with tears. We beg you to consider it. Director Standing Committee members Wang Xia, Wang Qinglan, Cheng Jinsheng, Standing Committee members Wu Yunqi, Shi Liangcai, Du Yuesheng, Lin Kanghou, Weng Yinchu, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Jin Houcheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Xi Yunsheng, Lu Bohong, Zhang Xiaoliang, Wang Binyan, Hu Bijiang, and Wen Lanting respectfully kowtow. The telegram to various charitable organizations is largely the same, so it is omitted.

Urgent Telegram Urging Rescue of Disaster Victims in Jiangbei 97

The Jiangsu Charity Relief Association received telegrams yesterday from Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner Zhang Zhijiang and Central Committee member Yu Jingtan, pleading for assistance on behalf of the disaster victims. In addition, Shen Zhuowu, a special commissioner of the Ministry of Railways, also telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday, urging it to instruct Dongtai and other counties to organize water disaster relief associations to rescue the people in the disaster area. The following is a transcription of the telegrams:

Zhang Zhijiang's Telegram

Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner Zhang Zhijiang telegraphed Shanghai, Tianjin, and Beiping yesterday, pleading on behalf of the disaster victims, saying, "To all relief associations:

This flood is an unprecedented catastrophe, and Jiangsu is a region with many waters, crisscrossed by rivers and dotted with lakes. The surge of torrential floods has caused particularly severe damage, and the number of affected people along the Yangtze River and Huai River is incalculable. The breach of the Grand Canal at Shaobo and Gaoyou in Jiangdu has resulted in the death of thousands more. According to a telegram from the Chamber of Commerce and Agriculture in the town, Shaobo is suffering from misfortune and calamities. Since the aftermath of the military disasters in 1927, it has suffered from severe droughts in 1928 and 1929, causing displacement and widespread suffering. In 1930, it finally had a harvest, and it was hoped that it could accumulate and recover. Unexpectedly, Heaven has not blessed us, and this year another flood has occurred, turning fields, tombs, and residences into marshes. Shaobo has suffered three catastrophes of drought, flood, and war, and the people are exhausted. In the event of a disaster, the suffering is greater than in other counties. Our benevolent commissioner, stationed in Yangzhou, has witnessed the devastation and understands the true situation. We have telegraphed charitable organizations in Shanghai, requesting relief and compassion. You are aware of the circumstances in our town. We implore the commissioner to continue to seek assistance from all parties and distribute relief funds as soon as possible, to alleviate the crisis and save lives. As the commissioner in charge of this region, I cannot stand idly by. I have previously telegraphed various charitable organizations, requesting generous assistance for relief. I am now making this further plea on behalf of countless disaster victims, urging all charitable organizations and kind-hearted people from all walks of life to consider the plight of the disaster victims who are starving and waiting for food, and to provide generous assistance so that they may be able to live again. This is what I, Zhijiang, will be praying for unceasingly. The telegram is urgent and I look forward to it anxiously." Zhang Zhijiang respectfully bows.

Yu Jingtan's Telegram

Central Committee member Yu Jingtan telegraphed Wang Yiting yesterday, saying, "To Wang Yiting: The flood in Jiangsu Province is a rare and severe disaster. Since the opening of the Three Dams in Guihai, Jiangbei, Xinghua, Taixian, Dongtai, and other counties have become marshes. Unfortunately, a sudden hurricane the other day caused the Grand Canal embankment to breach in more than ten places between Gaoyou and Shaobo, and millions of people in the downstream counties are in danger of drowning. Xinghua, which is located at the bottom of the cauldron, is suffering even more. I deeply admire your compassion for the farmers. I respectfully request that you send special commissioners to survey the area and provide relief, rice, straw mats, pots, and bowls to aid in the rescue. The people in the disaster area will be greatly benefited. I am pleading on their behalf, and I hope you will consider it." Yu Jingtan respectfully bows.

Gaoyou Compatriot Association's Telegram Pleading for Relief 98

"Most Urgent: Please forward to all charitable organizations. We read in the newspaper that there was a hurricane and rainstorm in Gaoyou on the 18th, and the three lakes of Hongze, Gaoyou, and Shaobo were roaring. At 5:00 AM on the same day, the Gaoyou city wall breached 50-60 zhang north of the Dangjun Tower, and the city wall south of Lujin also breached dozens of zhang. The water was fierce, and countless people died. After reading this, we are extremely shocked. We send this urgent telegram pleading for immediate assistance, saving those survivors by sending large sums of money, food, and boats to save lives. We are anxiously awaiting orders." The Shanghai Gaoyou Compatriot Association Preparatory Committee respectfully bows.

The Gaoyou Compatriot Association in Shanghai dispatched Ji Xiaozhou and Tong Junde to report to the Jiangsu Water Disaster Relief Association on the dire situation of the flood in Gao Shao.

(1) During the Qing Dynasty, the height of the Grand Canal embankment was one zhang and four chi. In the years of Daoguang 28 and Tongzhi 5, when the Qingshuitan breached, the water level in various places was only five or six chi. Now, the canal embankment has been increased to one zhang and eight chi, and temporarily added three chi, for a total of two zhang and one chi. The water level of these ten breaches is estimated to be at least one zhang and five or six chi. (2) In Gaoyou alone, according to the census report, the population is over 300,000. Adding the five counties below, the total is estimated to be around two or three million people. (3) The Gao Shao breach is unprecedented in history, unlike the gradual rise in water in the three towns of Wuhan. This water force is like Mount Tai pressing down, coming from nowhere and causing instant submersion, leaving people unable to escape, resulting in many deaths. (4) Today, our representatives are here to report, hoping that your association will quickly provide relief, have a large-scale overall plan, and also ask for help in forwarding the National Government and various charitable organizations, so that they can provide adequate relief. The representatives believe that the Gao Shao breach is a hundred times more serious than the floods in other parts of the country, and we ask your association to pay special attention and provide special relief.

Important News from the Water Disaster Relief Committee 99

The Accounting and Auditing Group Established

The Accounting and Auditing Group of the National Government Water Disaster Relief Committee held its inaugural meeting at the Bank of China at 12:00 noon on the 28th. The meeting was chaired by Zhang Jia'ao, the director of the group. Among those present were the Chinese and foreign members of the group, including Hubbard, Lawrence, Wardson, Lu Bohong, Song Hanzhang, Lin Kanghou, Bennett, Omura, and Zeng Rongpu. The "Regulations for the Accounting and Auditing Group of the National Government Water Disaster Relief Committee" were approved as follows: (1) The Accounting and Auditing Group shall perform the following duties: A. Review all "cash payment vouchers" and issue "payment certificates" to the treasury section of the finance group for payment to creditors or beneficiaries. No payment shall be made without a "payment certificate." B. Conduct regular audits of the treasury section's cash receipts and balances and certify them. C. Review all "relief material expenditure vouchers" and issue "material payment certificates" to the procurement section of the finance group, which may then issue relief materials to disaster victims. No relief materials shall be issued without a "material payment certificate." D. Conduct regular audits of the receipts and balances of relief supplies, including grain. E. Develop accounting and auditing systems and procedures for the committee. F. Prepare all financial reports required for the committee's affairs and responsibilities. All accounting records required for these reports shall be recorded and noted by the Accounting and Auditing Group, unless the Finance Group has separate records. G. Perform all other accounting and auditing functions of the committee. (2) The Accounting and Auditing Group may establish branch offices in each relief area to exercise its powers. These branch offices may include all relief agencies within their respective areas and shall be located at the same location as the financial branch offices in each area for cooperation. The financial branch offices in each area may be established upon the recommendation of the Accounting and Auditing Group. (3) Copies of all relief material allocation orders, purchase contracts and agreements, material receipts, invoices, payrolls, donation receipts, deposit slips, and bank statements of the committee shall be sent to the Accounting and Auditing Group for review. Before the format and procedures for the copies are determined, the relevant groups shall continue to send the original documents or copies of the documents to the Accounting and Auditing Group for review on a daily basis. (4) The Accounting and Auditing Group shall have the right to inquire about the financial situation from any officer of the committee when necessary. (5) The Accounting and Auditing Group shall submit all accounts and records to an accountant designated by the committee for audit. (6) Upon the completion of the committee's work, the Accounting and Auditing Group shall submit all books, records, and reports to the National Government's Audit Yuan or other designated government agency for filing. It was also resolved to establish a standing committee of the group, with the group's director, Wardson, and Song Hanzhang, as permanent members. It was also resolved that the group should conduct a detailed audit of the general accounts and accounts of each disaster area and publish a monthly report.

Chairman Zhang Jia'ao's Declaration

Chairman Zhang Jia'ao made the following declaration on behalf of the group: "The flood situation this year is serious. This committee has now established an Accounting and Auditing Group to audit all uses of flood relief donations. In the past, when there were natural disasters, relief funds were raised by charitable organizations or allocated by the government. The situation this year is exceptionally severe. We believe that past relief efforts may not have been perfect, and we should not repeat the same mistakes. Therefore, this committee has established a special group of Chinese and foreign accounting experts to conduct examinations on all expenditures related to relief funds, so as to increase the credibility of public opinion and ensure that relief funds are used properly. We hope that people from all walks of life will enthusiastically donate. This group is responsible for auditing and will always handle matters carefully to ensure that donations are used effectively and not wasted."

To Chairman Song of the Shanghai Water Disaster Relief Committee: At the annual meeting of this society, it was unanimously resolved to mobilize the entire membership of over 2,000 people to work hard to rescue and prevent disasters. If you need engineers to handle surveys and estimations, this society will assign members to come and serve at any time. Respectfully telegraphed by Wei Yifu, Hu Shuhua, Yan Deqing, etc. of the Chinese Engineering Society.

Urgent Telegram from the Hankou Branch Urging Remittance of Funds

The Hankou Sino-Foreign Relief Association telegraphed Shanghai yesterday, saying that the association had hired several sampans to work hard to rescue the disaster victims. The disaster victims gathered on high ground are fortunate to have escaped being buried alive, but they have no food to eat, and many people are gathered in one place, with foul air and steaming heat, which could lead to an epidemic. If one person becomes infected, it could spread, so the association is anxious to transport these disaster victims to disaster relief centers to ensure their safety and prevent the spread of disease. However, the work is very tense and the funds are extremely scarce. The Shanghai association is urged to quickly remit a large sum of money.

The Taizhou branch telegraphed that the disaster situation is becoming increasingly serious and the victims in the flooded areas are fleeing into the city, filling all public places such as schools and temples. These victims have no food or clothing and are in a terrible state. Please quickly allocate a large sum of money for relief.

Ningbo and Shaoxing Joint Rescue Association for the Hankou Disaster - News from Yesterday 103

The Ningbo and Shaoxing Joint Rescue Association for the Hankou Disaster received a telegram from Hankou yesterday, stating that the water had receded by an inch. The Ningo-Shaoxing ship will set sail on the morning of the 29th. They also received a letter from Director Yin in Hankou, stating that the water situation here has gradually receded and that according to surveys, it is not expected to rise again. People's hearts have also calmed down a little. Apart from a portion of the villagers who have taken the ship Ningo-Shaoxing directly back to Ningbo, there are others who are watching the water situation and deciding whether to advance or retreat, and there are also those who do not intend to return to their hometown. Even after the water recedes, the spread of immunity is most worrying. The association previously sent a telegram to various agencies and organizations when the ship Ningo-Shaoxing was about to sail to Ningbo, requesting that they arrange accommodation and repatriation when the ship arrives. Yesterday, the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce replied that upon receiving the telegram, they immediately joined the Supervision Office, the Yin County Government, and the Ningbo and Yin County Public Security Bureaus to organize the Ningbo and Shaoxing Joint Rescue Association for the Hankou Disaster Yin County Temporary Accommodation Office. Personnel from various agencies and organizations have been assigned to be responsible for handling the matter, and temples such as Yanging Guanzong have been designated as accommodation centers. As soon as the two ships, Ningo-Shaoxing arrive, they will be properly received and repatriated. At the same time, Customs Supervisor Jiang of Zhejiang also sent a reply to the association. It was also heard that the Moral Society had distributed 1,000 bottles of anti-epidemic medicine and planned to transport them to Hankou on Monday to help the fellow villagers of Ningbo and Shaoxing in Hankou, entrusted to the association for transportation. It was also heard that 167 villagers from Shaoxing boarded the ship Ningo-Shaoxing in Beijing to return to their hometown. However, the number of villagers from Ningbo is not yet reported. The association will hold a standing committee meeting at 3:00 PM on the 30th, and summons have been issued.

A Discussion on the Misery of Refugees from Mianyang 109

The Jianghua ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company previously carried a large number of refugees, who are now being accommodated by the Social Affairs Bureau, Public Security Bureau, Health Bureau, Tongren Fuyuantang, and others at Dongting Dongshan Hall on Fangxie Road and Zhai Zhenren Temple. Yesterday, the Health Bureau sent personnel to the two places to administer vaccinations. The refugees accommodated at Zhai Zhenren Temple were from Jiujiang, Jiangxi, numbering about 50. Those accommodated at Dongshan Hall were from Zhangjiagou, Mianyang, Hubei, numbering 100. It was said that the same ship carried more than this number, as a group had already disembarked when the ship stopped at Xiaguan. The disaster victims were pale and emaciated, with sunken cheeks and bloodshot eyes, and their miserable situation was indescribable. According to Yao Guoyi, the representative of the disaster victims from Mianyang, the flood had begun in early May, and by June 17, they knew that they could no longer stay and prepared food rations. The food was running out, and they had no choice but to leave the disaster area quickly. The fields in our area could have been harvested if the water had arrived a month later, but Heaven did not bless us, and we suffered this flood, turning the ripe fields into marshes. On June 20, we fled to Hankou in small boats and were accommodated in the accommodation. The accommodation was filled due to the rising water level, so three days ago, the office issued a symbol and boarded the Jianghua ship to Shanghai. Fortunately, each family of seven or three had no casualties. When we fled from our hometown to Hanyang, we often found floating corpses on the way. We shuddered and were terrified. Now, these people are all without blood, and the children do not have enough milk because their mothers are hungry and have no food, so the children are also pale and emaciated."

A resolution was passed to allocate 140 yuan from the fund, equivalent to half a day's wages for all members, to be sent to the Shanghai Bank for delivery to the disaster relief agencies for distribution.

Shanghai Christians Initiate Disaster Relief. The Christian Preaching Alliance convened an emergency meeting to discuss fundraising and relief measures, and notified Christians throughout the country to promote fundraising.

Jingwu Association Plans Disaster Relief. The Jingwu Athletic Association convened a special meeting on the 28th of this month to discuss fundraising methods. It was resolved to establish the "Shanghai Jingwu Fundraising and Relief Flood Disaster Committee" to manage the matter. In addition to an initial donation of 100 yuan from the association and vigorous fundraising efforts, (A) the association's Beijing branch will stage a theatrical performance to raise funds, with all expenses borne by the branch comrades. (B) Charity basketball and volleyball matches will be organized. All proceeds from tickets will be used for disaster relief.

Yishe Opera Troupe Schedules a Theatrical Performance for Disaster Relief. All members of the Yishe Opera Troupe have initiated a theatrical performance to aid disaster relief. It is scheduled for September 12th at the Grand Theater, featuring excerpts from Peking Opera. All proceeds from ticket sales will be used for disaster relief. All expenses will be fully borne by the members.

Elementary School Student Transfers Award for Disaster Relief. The Children's Reading Club of the Modern Bookstore on Fourth Malu in this city received a letter from member Jiang Mingzhi, stating his willingness to transfer his award of five yuan for disaster relief. Mr. Jiang, a student at Guangzhi Public School, is only eleven years old and is deeply concerned about the disaster situation, which is truly rare. It is reported that the association deeply appreciated Jiang's letter and decided to commend him in a reply. They also plan to request Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Wang Xiaolai, directors of the Modern Bookstore, to issue an honorary certificate to encourage him.

Ning-Shao Emergency Relief for the Wuhan Disaster 114

Report on the Actual Situation of the Wuhan Disaster 115

The First Batch of Over Two Thousand People Returns to Ningbo on the Xin Ningxing

The Second Batch of Over One Thousand People Departed from Wuhan Yesterday on the Yongxing Ship

The Ningbo Association in Shanghai, the Shaoxing Seven Counties Association, the Siming Public Hall, and other three organizations, recognizing that fellow villagers in Wuhan account for one-third of the business community, initiated an emergency relief effort for the Wuhan disaster. They have been holding meetings daily to raise funds and donate food. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Mr. Mao Heyuan and Hong Xuefan, the directors of the relief team sent to Hankou by the association, sent a letter from Hankou yesterday, providing a detailed report on the actual situation in the disaster area.

The Entire Team Arrived Safely in Wuhan. Our team departed from Shanghai on the Longhe ship on the 21st evening. We received a personal send-off from President Yu Qiaqing, Sun Meitang, and other fellow villagers. On the 24th, as the ship passed Nanjing, we held a meeting on board to discuss the approach. We organized the following ten sections: General Affairs Section, Documentation Section, Accounting Section, Hygiene Section, Discipline Section, Transportation Section, Liaison Section, General Affairs Section, Supply Section, and Reception Section. Each section has a section chief and several staff members. The entire team has over forty members. Hong Xuefan also serves as the chief of the General Affairs Section, and Zhang Yanling is in charge of the Liaison Section. We also agreed on various operating rules to adhere to and to facilitate relief efforts. As the ship passed Jiujiang upstream, we saw

Corpses Floating Down the River. Corpses, coffins, coffins, wooden houses, lumber, and appliances floated on the river, revealing the displacement and suffering of Wuhan residents. On the 25th, the ship arrived at Hankou. The local agent of the association, Yin Huichang, had pre-hired two small boats to greet the team members and transport medicines and food. A branch office was established at Yonghe Wheel, and Discipline Team leaders Xu Guanxiong and Yao Youbang, along with other team members, boarded over ten boats and conducted outreach on various streets. Within half a day, fellow villagers from Ningbo and Shaoxing gathered at the river docks. An estimated 1,500 people wished to return home by ship. Liaison Section leader Zhang Yanling contacted Chairman He of the General Headquarters regarding relief measures. The General Headquarters dispatched over ten military police officers and river police officers to protect the ship. Subsequently, because the disaster-stricken villagers could not wait any longer, the association used the pre-prepared Xin Ningxing ship in the morning of the 26th

Full of Fellow Villagers Returning Home. Medical care and medicine were provided on board, and no fares or tips were charged for any cabin class. As the ship was about to set sail, Directors Mao and Hong announced to the fellow villagers that they were very sorry for the late arrival of the relief and appointed Dong Xinqin, Bao Zhenfu, and two others as reception staff to accompany the ship. The fellow villagers were very grateful. The Xin Ningxing is scheduled to go directly to Ningbo. Those who transferred to Shanghai on the original ship were also not charged fares. Wuhan's weather is abnormal, and the air is full of pollutants, causing a gradual outbreak of epidemics. The association, recognizing this, established a temporary epidemic prevention clinic, headed by Dr. Xie Qigang. The clinic is temporarily located on the Yongxing ship. Each day, three to four hundred fellow villagers and non-villagers come to the clinic for treatment. Fortunately, the medicine supply is still sufficient to use. Since the arrival of the association's relief team in Wuhan, within two days, the people of Wuhan

Drew Great Attention. Although other disaster relief agencies have been established in Hubei Province, their spirit of dedication in rescue work is not as diligent as our association. Later, we cooperated with the National Government Relief Committee on the establishment of a shelter. The committee sent Mr. Li Zushen to Wuhan, residing at Room 4 of the Deming Hotel. Yin Huichang, Zhang Yanling, and Directors Mao Heyuan and Hong Xuefan went together to contact him. Mr. Li and Mr. Baker of the China International Famine Relief Commission were very supportive, saying that although the scope is different, the charitable nature is the same, and they are willing to help each other. Therefore, the association plans to temporarily establish a shelter for fellow villagers who are unwilling to return home and are impoverished. Starting on the 26th, the team dispatched a discipline team to take small boats to Wuhan to rescue fellow villagers from Ningbo and Shaoxing, and temporarily settled them in the Erxing ship. Unexpectedly, by the 27th, another six to seven hundred people had registered to return home. The association decided that the second relief ship, the Yongxing, would sail south on the 28th, with all fares waived. Because some team members accompanied the ship to Shanghai, it had to go directly to Shanghai. The staff members remaining in Wuhan are still actively carrying out relief work. In recent days, the water level in Wuhan has not increased or decreased. The central area is at 52.9 feet. However, the city's water and electricity supply are well managed and continue as usual, so the people are still relatively stable.

Ministry of Railways Circular 116

Grain Freight Fees Reduced 117

Due to the floods in various provinces and to maintain food supplies for the people, the Ministry of Railways has reduced freight fees. Yesterday, a special order was issued to the Jinghu and Huhu-Hangyong Railway Administrations: "Upon reviewing Article 123 of this year's National Commercial Transportation Conference, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce proposed that the fees for rice, barley, and wheat be changed from the originally designated fourth class to the fifth class to maintain food supplies for the people. This has been discussed and resolved at a meeting of the Freight Classification and Rate Committee of this ministry. It has also been promulgated to all railways by this ministry's Order No. 214, effective from August 1st of this year. Recently, continuous rains have caused severe flooding throughout the country, destroying farmland and leaving the people destitute. As the Minister of Railways deeply cares for the suffering of the people and urgently seeks to provide relief, it is now decided to maintain food supplies for the people. In accordance with Category 1 (Grains and Beans) of the Fifth Article of the Ordinary Goods Classification Table, except for eight items, including various flours, buckwheat flour, pea flour, rice flowers, rye, hemp seeds, and coffee beans, which are not produced in large quantities and are of higher value than rice and wheat, and thus do not need to be reduced in class; and except for bran and sorghum (unhulled), which are already classified as the fifth class and do not need to be reduced further, all other items, such as corn, five grains, sorghum, and wheat, will be uniformly reduced to the fifth class for fee collection. In addition to separate orders, two copies of the 'List of Reduced Classes for Coarse Grains' are attached. You are hereby ordered to comply and implement this measure, effective from September 1st of this year, and report back accordingly. This order."

Jiangsu Provincial Government Order 118

Wuxi Grain Allowed to Exit Normally 119

The Municipal Government Yesterday Received a Reply from the Jiangsu Provincial Government.

The Shanghai Municipal Government previously received a report from the Shanghai Rice Merchants' Association, stating that the Wuxi County Government, due to heavy rains and rising tides, had issued a notice prohibiting the export of grain at the request of the chief of the First District, which would affect the food supply in Shanghai. They requested assistance in addressing this issue. The Jiangsu Provincial Government was then consulted, requesting them to issue an order to all counties to allow the normal flow of grain to Shanghai. The Municipal Government received a reply from the Provincial Government yesterday, stating that the flow of grain within Jiangsu Province has always been permitted. The Wuxi County Government has been ordered to comply with the established regulations.

Delays in Hankou-Shanghai Exchange Rate Telegrams 124

Due to Congestion in Wireless Telegraph Service

The Shanghai Wireless Telegraph General Station of the Ministry of Communications responded to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday regarding the delays in Hankou-Shanghai exchange rate telegrams: "We have received your letter forwarded from the Hankou Chamber of Commerce, based on a letter from the Hankou Money Industry Association, stating that exchange rate telegrams to Shanghai are often delayed and contain discrepancies, leading to misunderstandings. They requested that the telegrams be sent and received immediately. This matter concerns the commerce of both cities. To maintain market information and stabilize public sentiment, we were instructed to forward and respond promptly to the situation. Upon investigation, land lines between Shanghai and Hankou have been disrupted recently, and all telegrams are being transmitted via wireless telegraphy. Therefore, the station's telegraph service is extremely congested. In addition, urgent official and military telegrams must be prioritized according to regulations, making it difficult to address ordinary telegrams. To avoid difficulties for both parties, we suggest that all money industry associations change to using express telegrams for such telegrams in the future to facilitate information. In addition to instructing all staff members to pay attention to this matter, we are responding to the previous letter. Please inform accordingly."

British Public Bus 125

Old Ticket Sellers Resume Work Yesterday 126

After the strike by all ticket sellers of the British Public Bus Company, the 110 old ticket sellers resumed work in the factory yesterday. The remaining 112 ticket sellers are still continuing the strike. According to the company, they have been dismissed. The various situations yesterday are recorded below:

Resumption of Work Yesterday. 110 old ticket sellers resumed work at the main factory on Kang Naot Road yesterday. Public buses on all routes were fully operational. The routes that were shortened due to the strike were also fully restored. Twelve buses on Route 1 (Jing'an Temple to Gongyuan Shooting Range), ten buses on Route 2 (Eryang Jingqiao to Gongyuan Shooting Range), six buses on Route 5 (Sanmaoge Bridge to North Railway Station), eighteen buses on Route 9 (Jing'an Temple to Electric Light Factory), and fourteen buses on Route 10 (Caojiadu to Yinxiangxiang). However, Routes 3, 4, 6, and 7 have not yet been restored because the number of returning workers is half of the original number. These routes will be restored after newly recruited ticket sellers are fully trained.

Resolution. The result of the negotiations between the old ticket sellers and driver representatives with the company manager the day before yesterday was unconditional resumption of work. Each ticket seller went to report for duty and was selected by the company. A total of 165 people reported for duty, and 110 were selected. The company stated that the remaining 112 have been completely dismissed and will not be rehired. However, the one hundred or so people who have not resumed work stated that they are still continuing the strike and hope to achieve final victory.

Chen Hangshu, the younger brother of Chen Bulei, Vice Minister of Education, who served as the secretary and lecturer of Guanghua University, went to France in 1927 to study economics at the University of Paris. Such a talented and learned scholar who did not live long is deeply mourned not only by his old friends.

Local News

Promoting Chinese Culture: The Chinese English Drama Society 132

Organized by Young Chinese Men and Women

All Dialogue in the Plays is in English

Western customs view the number thirteen as unlucky, and people avoid it as if escaping something dreadful, fearing misfortune. If thirteen people undertake a joint venture on a Friday, the prospects are so dire that words cannot describe them. This is because thirteen is considered an unlucky number, and Friday is also seen as a day of misfortune. However, in Shanghai, there is the Chinese English Drama Society, organized by a group of young men and women with new ideas. They specialize in performing Chinese opera entirely in English, allowing Westerners to deeply understand the noble culture of our country's past and the inherent virtues of our social life. This type of theatrical performance was previously seen only in a few schools, and its prevalence was not widespread, failing to attract attention. Therefore, this Chinese English Drama Society is not only the first of its kind in Shanghai, but also unique nationwide. The society was established on a Friday in May of this year, with thirteen founding members, which, according to Western customs, could be considered the height of misfortune. However, in the past three months, it has progressed smoothly and accomplished great things. Recently, it has become known for publicly performing the famous play "Xi Shi," and its enterprising spirit is highly commendable. It can also be asserted that this group of young men and women are by no means infatuated with Western life.

The purpose of the Chinese English Drama Society is to perform ancient Chinese culture, allowing Westerners to accurately understand our country's long history and ancient social life through drama. For the drama society itself, it aims to elevate the thinking of young people, enabling them to express the characteristics of our excellent nation at any time and to enhance international friendship. The words and dialogues used in the plays are purely in English, so that Western theatergoers have no difficulty in understanding. Its first public performance is set to be the play "Xi Shi." Xi Shi is a representative of Chinese female beauty and has long been admired by Westerners. With this play's performance, it is expected that Westerners' praise of Xi Shi will undergo another transformation in perspective.

Since the society was established only three months ago, many people in Shanghai may not yet know its nature and organization. This drama society is entirely amateur in nature, and its purpose has been fully stated above. The president is Mrs. Ma Jiashou, and Mrs. Guo Anci serves as the vice president, both of whom are well-known figures in Shanghai's women's circles and have a reputation in social circles. The secretary is Mr. Shi Zhaokang, the treasurer is Mr. Zhou Fanping, and there are currently more than thirty members, all of whom have received high-level education and can speak fluent English. The society's expenses are borne by well-known Shanghai businessmen and bankers, and members are also required to pay a considerable monthly membership fee. Regular meetings are held every half month, and performances are not scheduled regularly. Many famous figures in the literary world both domestically and abroad support this society, and it is said that Dr. Hu Shi is also one of them.

The date of the public performance of "Xi Shi" is now set for mid-November. According to important officials in the society, the play is based on the book "Xi Shi" written by Mrs. Wu Liande. The play's words and dialogues are written by Mr. Zhou Fanping, Mr. Li Shimin, Mrs. Ma Jiashou, and Mr. Shi Zhaokang. The material is carefully selected, and the plot is excellent, striving to be consistent with ancient culture. The entire play has now been completed, and rehearsals will begin in two weeks. Mrs. O'Hara from the United States has been invited as the director and consultant. Mrs. O'Hara is meticulous in drama and has twenty years of stage experience. With this expert directing the play, its effectiveness and emotional depth will be further enhanced.

The future success of this society is within our expectations. Although the play has not yet been performed publicly, its reputation has already attracted considerable attention. European and American drama experts particularly admire it, as Westerners who study Chinese drama often lack adequate guidance. The organization of this society is truly the closest stepping stone. What is particularly gratifying for us about this society is that its stated purpose and the dramas it intends to perform are all things that Westerners have long desired but could not obtain. Therefore, since the announcement of the society's establishment, representatives of various foreign film companies stationed in Shanghai have been instructed by their headquarters to request to film talking movies of the society, which is also sufficient to show its position in the theatrical world.

The Completion of the Dike Repair in Songpu Towns is Limited to a Specific Date 133

The 18th day of the lunar seventh month is the date of high tide.

The Public Works Bureau Increases Labor and Sends Personnel to Supervise

The dikes set up in Wusong Yunzaobang and Pudong Gaoqiao, two towns, have been in place for years and are the two main dikes to resist the tide from entering the town. A few days ago, after heavy rains in Shanghai, the tide rose, and the dikes in both towns were severely damaged by the surge. Recently, the Municipal Public Works Bureau ordered workers to repair and build them. There are more than 2,000 workers on the Gaoqiao Dike and more than 800 people in the Yunzaobang area, working to repair, build, and fill the breaches, placing a large number of sandbags between the dikes. The bureau also sent personnel to the towns to supervise the work, rushing to complete the construction within two days. Every autumn, the tide in the Huangpu River is more intense than the usual monthly tide, and the 18th day of the lunar seventh month is the day when the biggest tide of the year begins. Therefore, the bureau specially increased labor yesterday and actively carried out the construction.

The Disaster Situation in Various Sands Outside Wusong Estuary is Serious 134

The Embankments are Completely Collapsed and the Houses are Completely Destroyed

More Than a Hundred Sand Dwellers Died Tragically and Countless are Missing

Changxing Sand, Ping'an Sand, Shitou Sand, Ruifeng Sand, Yongxing Sand, Dingxing Sand, and Chongbin Sand, which belong to the first district of Baoshan, are all small islands in the sea outside the Wusong Estuary. The total number of residents is more than a thousand, all of whom rely on farming for a living. This time, due to the hurricane and torrential rain, the angry tide rose sharply, and the embankments of each island were completely collapsed. The water depth in the flat ground was more than ten feet. Fortunately, the seawater soon receded, but eight or nine out of ten houses were destroyed, and more than one hundred farmers drowned. Countless people are missing, and the fields and crops are almost completely submerged. Those who escaped have no home to return to and are waiting to be fed. Now, after the tide, due to the lack of embankment defense, the seawater rises and recedes from time to time, and the disaster victims are trapped in the water, suffering from hunger and cold. The situation is extremely tragic. County Magistrate Zhao Enju and Wang Qingtao, the chief of the first district, immediately sent people by boat to each sand to carry out rescue and accommodation separately after receiving the report. County Magistrate Zhao also ordered Wang Decheng, the chief of political affairs and police, to investigate the disaster situation, which was extremely serious. In the past two days, more than a dozen floating corpses were successively washed to the sea embankment outside the east gate of Baoshan and outside the north fort of the fortress, all of which were collected by the charitable hall. County Magistrate Zhao and District Chief Wang urgently telegraphed the provincial hall and the National Flood Relief Association yesterday, requesting them to find ways to provide relief and release emergency relief.

Case of Impersonating Officials to Privately Purchase Military Supplies 135

The Chinese and Russian People Were Convicted Yesterday

The Russian Bik Laviskai and the Chinese Wei Xiaolan were previously charged with conspiring to impersonate officials of the National Government to order military supplies worth 1.9 million yuan from the Laifa Foreign Firm on Guangdong Road, and forging documents and seals with the intention of defrauding money. The case was uncovered, and they were arrested by the Chinese detective Ma Wenda and the Western detective Beibeining of the General Patrol Room. Attorney Ru Baoyi represented the patrol room and filed a public prosecution in the First District Court in accordance with Articles 165, 224, 234, and 370 of the Criminal Law. The Special Court had summoned the parties several times, and the details had been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the date for the verdict arrived. The patrol room attorney Ru Baoyi, the attorney Qiu Fenling representing Bik Laviskai, and the attorney Fan Gang representing Wei Xiaolan all appeared in court to await the verdict. At around 9 o'clock, Judge Xu Jiashi, the presiding judge of the criminal court, took the seat of the first criminal court and announced the verdict. The main text of the verdict stated that Laviskai was sentenced to nine months of imprisonment for impersonating a public official of the Republic of China with the intention of extorting property, and five months of imprisonment for forging documents and seals, with a total sentence of one year of imprisonment. Bik was sentenced to one year of imprisonment for jointly impersonating a public official of the Republic of China with the intention of extorting property. Wei Xiaolan was sentenced to two months of imprisonment for assisting in the intention of extorting property. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized was allowed to be offset against the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The contract, the duplicate of the contract, the bill of lading, the draft of the bill of lading, a piece of paper, and a seal were confiscated.

More Than a Thousand Mu of Farmland in Yinhang Were Submerged 136

River Water Overflowed, Drowning Nineteen Farmers

The Social Bureau is Handling Relief for Homeless Disaster Victims

According to the Guowen News Agency, the section of Jungong Road in the Yinhang District of Shanghai, from East Yangshupu to Jiansong Bridge, was overflowed by the tide and rain on the night of the 26th, and the riverbank of Jiansong Bridge rushed in, causing more than a thousand mu of sandy beaches outside the embankment and farmland inside the embankment to be submerged. The thatched houses on the beach were also swept away by the waves. Yesterday, it was learned that a total of nineteen people were tragically drowned. The families of others living on the beach were swept into the Huangpu River by the waves, and there has been no investigation so far. The Social Bureau, through the Yinhang Municipal Committee Office, reported the disaster relief and requested the Public Works Bureau to repair the embankments as soon as possible. As a result, the Social Bureau sent Zhou Minggang and Yan Wenkai to investigate the disaster for several days.

The First District of the County Reported the Situation of Wind and Rain Disaster 137

Wu Jingqing, the chief of the first district (Minhang) of the county, reported to the county government, saying, (the above is omitted) "On the 24th of this month, a sudden gale and torrential rain came from the southeast, its momentum was turbulent and unstoppable, and it lasted for two days and nights before it subsided. It was found that the cotton was just setting bolls, and after this blow, it was almost completely scattered. Most of the rice was still in bloom, and after this catastrophe, it will also bloom without bearing fruit, and the autumn harvest is completely hopeless. As for the sheds and huts in various villages, countless were toppled and collapsed. Several houses in the town were also blown down, such as the Jin family's kitchen in Hengjing Beach, the walls of the Public Security Bureau, and the gardens along the Minyuan River. Other telephone poles and fences were also blown down a lot. After the wind and rain, the river tide rose, the water level was several feet above the ground, and the huge waves surged, causing the eastern Miaowan revetment in Min Town to be washed away for more than ten feet. The flood flooded in, causing panic among the people in the town. The sundries of each family along the river drifted away with the waves, and the boats on the Huangpu River were overturned by the waves everywhere. In the Huangpu River, the sound of crying was deafening. In summary, the magnitude of this disaster is unprecedented in history. The cotton and rice have suffered a poor harvest, and the houses have been blown down. Thinking of the people's livelihood, I feel shivering. In addition to jointly devising remedial measures with the heads of various villages and towns, and making every effort to repair the riverbank, I also submit a separate request for subsidies. Therefore, I hereby report the information, and I pray that you will consider providing relief, which is for the public convenience."

The Post Office Asks Senders in This City to Pay Attention 138

The Street Name Must Include the Words "Shanghai" or "This City"

It is heard that the Shanghai Postal Administration has noted that many streets in this city are named after foreign provinces or cities, such as Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road, which are already well known to everyone, but more remote places, such as Haizhou Road, Hejian Road, Liaoyang Road, Qiqihar Road, and Qingdao Road, are still not familiar to many. When the public hands over local delivery mail, they often omit the words "Shanghai" or "This City" on the street name, which easily leads to misidentification as mail intended for foreign cities during sorting, inevitably causing delays. It is now planned to notify the public that all local delivery mail must include the words "Shanghai" or "This City" before the street name to avoid misdelivery.

Zicha and others are small businesses and are very afraid of getting involved in lawsuits. They only filed a countersuit in accordance with Article 356 of the Criminal Procedure Law because they were being too severely persecuted and could no longer bear it. The court should declare Zicha and others innocent and investigate the defendants in the countersuit in accordance with the law. It is heard that this countersuit case will also be resolved at the same time tomorrow.

Gu Dingying and His Wife Fined 200 Yuan 148

Guilty of Depriving Their Brother of Freedom of Action

The woman Gu Ai hired a lawyer yesterday and criminally sued in the Second Special District Court, stating that the plaintiff's husband, Gu Dingrui, i.e., Gu Apin, was summoned by his younger brother Gu Dingying and his wife Cai on the 20th of last month at 12:00 noon, and was privately tortured, hung up, and forced to write a note for 5,000 yuan. After that, the plaintiff's husband suddenly disappeared and his life and death are unknown to this day. Under these circumstances, the defendant couple actually violated Articles 316 and 318 of the Criminal Law, obstructing freedom and forcing injury. She requested that they be interrogated in accordance with the law and requested an incidental private prosecution, etc. Then the plaintiff Gu Ai said that her husband Dingrui had been summoned by the defendants and has been missing for more than a month, and there is no news of him. However, the situation of her husband being privately tortured, hung up, and forced to write a note by the defendants was witnessed and can be testified by the female servant Zhu Bao. She requested a strict investigation. Gu Dingying ·

Gu Ai · both claimed that it was because his brother Ding secretly sold the property jointly owned by the people, obtaining 25,000 taels of silver, and used it alone. When the property owners learned of this, they went to his brother Dingrui's father's place and told him to hand over the money for equal distribution. At that time, Dingrui had no money to hand over, so he was asked to write a note, but there was no coercion or torture. They also hired a lawyer to defend them, saying that the two crimes accused by the plaintiff had no evidence. The plaintiff's husband actually ran away because he was afraid of dividing the property. If his father had more than one million in property to divide, the plaintiff's husband would immediately come forward. What he sued was unfounded and requested a rejection. At this point, the prosecutor stood up and expressed his opinion, saying that the defendants' behavior of obstructing freedom in Article 316 was obvious, but the crime of forcing injury in Article 318 required conclusive evidence and a complaint from the person concerned before it could be established. Judge Ge immediately announced the court's judgment that the defendants Gu Dingying · Gu Ai · together were each fined two yuan for the crime of depriving collateral relatives of freedom of action by illegal means. The remaining number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized was offset against the fine at a rate of one day for two yuan. The remaining parts of the lawsuit were all innocent. The plaintiff's lawsuit in the incidental civil suit was rejected.

Publication of the Veritable Records of Zheng Chenggong 162

Zheng Chenggong, Prince Yanping of Ming Dynasty, fought against the Manchus and opened up Taiwan at the end of the Ming Dynasty.

His great achievements are worthy of being a great national hero. However, the records of his life were mostly slanderous in the official Qing Dynasty records, and the writings of private individuals were mostly based on hearsay and unreliable. Fortunately, Yang Ying, the director of the Ministry of Revenue under Yanping at that time, compiled the Veritable Records based on his personal observations, recording events year by year and month by month in detail. The records are particularly detailed on military and financial matters. Among them, Yanping's letters to the Manchus and his father, Zhilong, are full of loyalty and righteousness, and seven or eight out of ten are not found in other books, making them particularly valuable. The book was secretly treasured by Zheng's descendants for generations. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, Wu Huqian, the battalion commander of Qin Wangshan's army of the Fujian Autonomous Army, obtained it in Nan'an Shijing Township, the former residence of Yanping. Qin entrusted it to Li Hanqing, the director of the Xiamen Kulangsu Private Zhongshan Library, for collation and preservation. Recently, Li obtained Qin's consent to entrust the Institute of History and Philology of the National Academia Sinica to photographically reproduce the original book, so that this credible history can be circulated among people. The original name of the book was Veritable Records of Yanping, but the institute changed it to "Veritable Records of Yang Ying, the Yanping Household Official's Conquest," and Zhu Xizu wrote a long preface to authenticate it. It has now been published, and each copy is sold for two silver dollars. All branches of the Commercial Press in various cities are acting as agents. This is also a fortunate event for national history.

Calligrapher Tan Yunshan recently initiated a book donation to help with disaster relief for the floods in Guangdong Province. Letter

Ministry of Education Issues Circular to Provinces to Universally Establish Agricultural, Medical, and Engineering Schools 166

And Implementation Plans for Establishing Secondary Agricultural and Industrial Schools

The Ministry of Education issued circulars to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities regarding the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city, as approved by the central government, and the implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city.

The circular stated: "It has been investigated that the Ministry has drafted implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city, and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and approval. One, the case was instructed by the Executive Yuan No. 3212 (instructed by the National Government No. 337, the previous report from the said Yuan reported that the Ministry of Education drafted implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city, and requested forwarding for review and approval, etc., to the government, which was then sent to the Central Political Conference. Now, approval has been received in reply, after being submitted to the Education and Finance Groups for review, it was reported that the study period for medical specialized schools in the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city should be changed to four years. Moreover, since Hankou City has been changed to a city not directly subordinate to the Executive Yuan, Hankou City in the attached table of the original draft should be changed to the column for cities with a population of over 300,000. The rest can be passed as reviewed, etc., which was resolved by the 276th meeting of this conference in accordance with the review opinions. Accordingly, the case is recorded and the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and the implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city, as passed by the meeting, are attached, and you are instructed to comply, etc. In accordance with this, the original documents are copied and issued, and the Yuan is instructed to comply and implement accordingly.' In accordance with this, the original documents are copied and issued, instructing the said department to immediately comply and implement accordingly," etc. Enclosed are copies of the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and the implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city. It should be noted that the study period for medical specialized schools as stipulated in the revised regulations for specialized schools is three years. After completing the three-year curriculum, there will be a one-year internship. Moreover, based on the recent recommendation of the Medical Education Committee of this department, it is requested that the study period be set at three years. Now, it has been instructed that the study period for medical specialized schools in the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city, as resolved by the Central Political Conference, should be changed to four years. Can it still be set at three years plus an additional year of internship? This was submitted and instructed by the Executive Yuan No. 4033: "The National Government No. 404 instruction is to be complied with. The previous report from the said Yuan reported that the Ministry of Education presented the case of the study period for medical specialized schools in the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city. The 276th meeting of the Central Political Conference resolved to change it to four years. Can it still be set at three years plus an additional year of internship? We earnestly request that you review and instruct us to comply, etc., to the government, which was then sent to the Central Political Conference. Now, approval has been received in reply, and it has been submitted to the 283rd meeting for discussion and resolved that the resolution of the 276th meeting of this conference should still be complied with and need not be modified. A special record is made and sent to you for your reference and compliance, etc. In accordance with this, the Yuan is instructed to comply and implement accordingly, this order, etc. In accordance with this, in addition to reporting, the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and the implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city are urgently copied and issued, instructing the said department to comply and implement accordingly. In addition, since the study period for medical specialized schools has been stipulated as four years, with an additional year of internship after completion of studies, the study period for specialized schools as stipulated in the Specialized School Organization Law promulgated by the National Government should be revised by this department in a separate document. The study period for medical specialized schools as stipulated in the revised regulations for specialized schools promulgated by this department will also be corrected immediately, and this department will submit a separate document for record. Also, the names of secondary agricultural and industrial schools should be determined by this department after the names of vocational schools are finalized, and then ordered to be complied with separately, and you should be informed, this order. Copies of the implementation plans for the universal establishment of agricultural, medical, and engineering specialized schools in each province and city and the implementation plans for the establishment of secondary agricultural and industrial schools in each province and city are attached (Editor's note: The complete plan has been recorded in the August 21st and 23rd editions of this column)."

The current government is only borrowing wheat to provide food for the people, but it also needs to borrow cotton to provide clothing for the people. Municipal Education Bureau Takes Over Private Rural First Elementary School 169

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau previously received a joint petition from citizens Li Keping and Liu Xuechu of Shenxing Town, Yinhang District, requesting that the private Rural First Elementary School, which had been closed, be taken over by the city to facilitate children's enrollment. After sending personnel to investigate and reply, it was found that there were many school-age children in the area, and the closure of the school did cause many children to be out of school. The closed private Rural First Elementary School has now been taken over by the Municipal Education Bureau and renamed the Municipal Rural Elementary School. Two classrooms have been temporarily set up for teaching, and Wang Renmin has been temporarily appointed as the acting principal of the school.

俵氏 (Hyooji) Wins Against Qiu Feihai with a Score of Three to One 175

丨 Hyooji Sekio Lives Up to His Reputation as a Renowned Player 丨

(6丨2)

Hyooji Sekio (Japan) (6丨1) Qiu Feihai (China)

(3丨6)

(6丨4)

Qiu and Hyooji are both giants among Shanghai's tennis players, and also national players for China and Japan. Their superb skills are obvious to all. However, people are eager to know how much each has improved in the past year. Yesterday, both players, bearing the mission of representing their countries, participated in the first singles match of the Rotary Cup final. They gave their all to bring glory to their country and compete for personal honor, which was inevitable. The more than a thousand spectators were not there by chance. After a great battle, Hyooji Sekio surprisingly defeated Qiu Feihai by a score of three to one. The audience regarded it as a result of skill, not luck. Mr. Qiu shook hands to congratulate him, also sighing in admiration.

On average, Hyooji excelled in defending the baseline, hitting shots left and right, both offensively and defensively. He occasionally went to the net and showed good control, ran quickly, and had a powerful serve, which was his specialty. Mr. Qiu's favored forehand shots were not seen as often, and sometimes he tried to use them, which felt formidable. However, his serves were missed, and his footwork was slow, which was the main reason for his defeat. However, he was good at using clever force, often using softness to overcome hardness, which Hyooji could not avoid. On average, Hyooji was superior.

The two heroes, in a situation of "deep water and scorching fire," entered the arena holding their rackets, receiving a warm welcome from the audience. After a brief warm-up, the battle began. Mr. Qiu took to the court to gain momentum, but was intercepted by Hyooji, resulting in a score of two. In the third game, Mr. Qiu used all his skills to control the overall situation, moving left, right, forward, and backward at will, seeming to have returned to the golden age when he first came to China. Applause was endless, and he was at the peak of his success. He secured the third game. However, after this, Hyooji was superior in every way, plunging Mr. Qiu into a state of "deep water and scorching fire." He completed eight games in one go, winning the first set six to two. He then took a three-to-zero lead in the second set. Mr. Qiu struggled to cope, initially winning back one game, but then a storm suddenly arrived, like a body after being robbed and brutally ravaged. The subsequent three games unexpectedly went to Hyooji again, making him the victor. Hyooji won the second set six to one again.

Trying to Reverse Misfortune, Mr. Qiu lost two sets. The audience was worried about him, but Mr. Qiu remained calm, showing a spirit of reversing misfortune. He was energetic and strong. After two games, he won two more games, constantly striving forward without setbacks. Hyooji was trapped under the opponent's powerful hand, allowing himself to be whittled away. In the end, with a score of three to six, he lost the third set to Mr. Qiu. After a ten-minute break, the fourth set began. Mr. Qiu, despite losing with a score of zero to three, managed to win a game. The audience's spirits soared, congratulating each other. In the second game, he cleanly won again, causing a great shout, as if victory was within reach. Hyooji's expression changed. He perked up and tied the score at two-two. Then, Mr. Qiu won another game, and Hyooji tied it again, even surpassing him. Mr. Qiu showed his power, tying the score at four-four. At that time, the situation was tense, and the atmosphere changed. Mr. Qiu's misfortune came again, losing two consecutive games, eventually losing the fourth set with a score of four to six.

Jiang Daozhang Wins Against Machida Only After Five Sets 176

丨 Jiang Daozhang Had a Hard Time 丨

(Six to Two)

Jiang Daozhang (China) (Six to Four) Machida (Japan)

(Three to Six)

(Zero to Six)

(Seven to Five)

The battle between Jiang Daozhang and Machida was crucial in the final. If Jiang won against Machida, the Chinese team would still have a chance in the doubles match. Since Qiu could not win both singles matches, if Jiang lost to Machida, even if China won the doubles, it would be in vain. Therefore, after Qiu's defeat, the attention of the entire audience was focused on Jiang and Machida. Fortunately, Jiang Daozhang finally defeated Machida amidst the rough seas and dangerous waves, carving out a path to survival for the Chinese team.

Slightly Lacking Control, based on Jiang's qualifications and skills, Machida was not his opponent. However, after smoothly winning two sets, Jiang suffered two consecutive defeats, giving the Japanese a chance to win. Moreover, in the fifth set, when Jiang had an excellent lead of five to two, he allowed Machida to tie the score at five to five. The reason was none other than his lack of control. Jiang consistently outperformed Machida in serving, hitting, and intercepting, and gave a wonderful performance in the first two sets. As for Machida, he displayed purely Japanese strengths, excelling in baseline rallies and possessing great stamina. When we look at his skills from last year and the rapid progress he has made this autumn, we cannot help but be amazed. In short, Jiang Daozhang was able to salvage the final victory from a slump, which can only be described as fortunate.

Sudden Turmoil, Machida served first, and Jiang won consecutively, winning three games. Machida only won the fourth and fifth games. In the first set, Jiang won decisively with six to two. In the second set, Jiang continued to use powerful angled shots, baseline rallies, and net interceptions, taking a commanding lead of five to two. Although Machida won two more games, Jiang still won again with six to four. Unexpectedly, amidst a smooth sailing, shocking waves and furious tides suddenly arose before him, and the firm and strong foundation suddenly showed signs of shaking. People were panic-stricken, wondering if there was a chance for survival. In the third set, Jiang fell behind with three to four, and then lost ten consecutive games, losing the third set with three to six, and the fourth set with zero to six in a devastating defeat. Thus, the life of the Chinese team depended on this final set.

Victory Amidst Danger, the fifth set began, and the sky was already growing dark. Qiu Feihai had already declared his defeat. Both Jiang and Machida were exhausted, and no one was sure who would win. Machida took a lead of two to zero. Everyone wondered whether Jiang could win. Jiang Daozhang, realizing the importance of his mission, rallied his spirits and exerted all his remaining strength, hitting hard and putting on heavy pressure, winning five consecutive games, creating a confident lead of five to two. However, after the fierce attack, he overexerted himself, and his control was poor. The ball touched the net one after another, and Machida suddenly tied the score at five to five. Dusk had already fallen, the light was very poor.

The two competed for victory and defeat in the dim evening light. After the two games were tied several times, Jiang finally won the final victory with seven to five, making the total score three to two.
