Free Talk

A Word of Insight 182

— Mengdie

The organization of an entire family consists of those who are naturally united, such as fathers and sons, brothers, and those who are united by human effort, such as mothers-in-law and daughters-in-law, husbands and wives. Theoretically, those united by human effort are difficult to unite, but the easiest to unite are husbands and wives. Therefore, love is omnipotent. Those naturally united are easy to unite, but the most difficult to unite are brothers. Therefore, money is the root of all evil.

The maintenance of ethics is rooted in a single word: love. However, only parents' love for their children is unconditional. They do not love their children only after they are virtuous and filial. Even if they know that their children will grow up to be unfilial, they still love them. Other relationships, such as husbands and wives, are based on conditional love. There is no such thing as a one-sided relationship. Why do people love their wives more than their parents? Isn't this a reversal of priorities?

Everyone has their abilities and inabilities. This statement is most accurate. It shows that people's talents are not superior or inferior, but only differ in the focus of their effort. Consider the masters of Weiqi and Mahjong. They did not achieve their skills overnight. If they applied their effort to studying, then the gamblers would all be respected scholars.

Ancient Beast Teeth 183

— Moyi

Mr. Anders, an American zoologist and leader of the Central Asian expedition, recently published an article in the London Illustrated News about the discovery of teeth of extinct ancient beasts. I have translated it as follows for the study of archaeologists.

About two million years ago, there was a large lake in eastern Mongolia, almost as large as present-day Lake Michigan (Lakemicbigan, located in North America with an area of 25,600 square miles). It was discovered by the Central Asian Exploration Team in the summer of 1928. Of course, the lake water had dried up, and only a few traces of the lake shore could be faintly seen. We stayed there for two weeks. Mr. Schell, a geologist, excavated a flat, basin-like object, about ten inches long, eight inches wide, and three-quarters of an inch thick. After repeated study, we realized that it was a tooth. But we were still in the dark about what kind of animal's tooth it was. We continued to excavate, and within three days, we excavated more than a dozen of them.

Later, we returned to Beiping, then to Shanghai, and returned to the United States. After research by archaeologists in various countries, it was determined that it was the giant tooth of an extinct ancient beast. In the United States, we continued to study for two years. Many famous archaeologists unanimously confirmed that it was this type of tooth. There were quite a few. So, in the spring of 1930, our entire team returned to the original location to explore.

Our tents were still stationed on the lake shore. In front of the tents, there was a small river crossing in the distance. Behind us was a large desert. There, in addition to small antelopes, there were no Mongolians. Wolves often attacked us in packs all over the mountains and fields. Fortunately, we all had guns, and we even killed twenty or thirty wolves at once. Only then did their momentum subside slightly. So we call it "Wolf Village." But the small antelopes were very beneficial to us. We considered their milk to be a supreme beverage.

One day, about six miles from the tents, we excavated six molars of giant beasts, even larger than those excavated in 1928. Therefore, we concluded that this must be a cemetery where giant beasts buried their teeth. But because this place was not soil, but very solid rock, it was difficult to excavate, let alone for people. Even using explosives to blast it felt difficult. But we didn't dare to use explosives, fearing that it would damage our objective. There was no way to think about it. We could only chop the stones little by little, like carving. Thus, the secrets of three million years ago were revealed to us.

After more than two months of excavation work, we obtained a large number of teeth, some shaped like stone mortars, some shaped like , and some shaped like spoons. We also excavated many ribs, vertebrae, skulls, and bones of the limbs. We put them together like jigsaw puzzles to form forty terrifying ancient beasts (all males). Their shape was similar to the elephants we commonly see now, but their massive bodies were far beyond that.

In another place, we also discovered many young and female giant beasts. According to experts, when this lake did not dry up at first, there were probably many young giant beasts who came to drink water and unfortunately fell and drowned. Their mothers also sacrificed their lives to save their little lives. So, there were quite a few females as well. Therefore, it was also determined that they were mammals, which is evidenced by the fact that there are many mammals there today, such as small antelopes, foxes, wolves, and carnivores. Perhaps it is not very arbitrary.

Strange News Amidst the Flood 184

— Hong Qian

The severity of this year's flood and the vastness of the affected areas are truly unprecedented in a century. As a result, all kinds of strange and unusual events have occurred that are beyond expectations. I recently met a returnee from a river port who talked about the Wang family's three children who drifted three hundred miles in front of the Wangjiang Tower during the flood. It was particularly shocking. If you meet a superstitious person, they will definitely say that there is divine protection in the dark. I will record its beginning and end as follows.

The three Wang children are brothers. Their original hometown is Wanggang, She County. Their father's name is Jian Tai, who is a boatman by profession. The eldest son is named Tian Zhao, who is sixteen years old. The second son is named Tian Pei, who is fourteen years old. The third son is named Tian Song, who is twelve years old. The fourth son is named Tian Bai, who is only eight years old. On this day, because an old boat was being repaired in the river about ten miles away from Wanggang, Jian Tai and his wife and several children went to supervise the work. Tian Song alone did not go with them. Later, Jian Tai and his wife also returned home. Tian Zhao, Tian Pei, and Tian Bai stayed there. That place was originally a tributary of a large river. The river surface was narrow and shallow, and it was often dry. But this year, there was a lot of rain, and the ditches were all full, so the boat could be repaired. The boat workers were negligent and did not tie the cable. They thought that this large boat was moored in a small river, so they did not expect anything else to happen. When it was dusk, they sat on the bow of the boat to cool off. The sky suddenly changed, the wind rose and the clouds surged. They heard the sound of water like thunder. Before long, the flood swelled up, as if overturning mountains and toppling seas, rushing in torrents. The boat was suddenly lifted up and could not control itself. Everyone was frightened and lost their heads. They each took oars on their backs and fled, no longer able to care for the three children. The three children ran down into the cabin, with no way to escape. They only felt that the waves were turbulent and the boat was rising and falling, drifting with the water. They did not know how many miles they had traveled. They also hit the rocks several times, and both ends were broken. The three children suddenly found a plank in the crisis. Tian Zhao and Tian Pei each straddled one end, and Tian Bai, who was young, happened to be in the middle. Tian Zhao and Tian Pei held hands to prevent Tian Bai from falling. So they floated and sank, letting it go where it would. In one night, they drifted to the Wangjiang Tower in Hekou. Hekou is a riverside market. The upper reaches of the Han River were also flooded. Ordinary ruffians saw countless pieces of furniture and boxes drifting from the upper reaches. They were scrambling to take small boats to salvage them. From a distance, they saw a huge object drifting from the upper reaches. They couldn't tell what it was and were overjoyed. They thought they could make a big fortune. Who knew that when they got closer, it was a plank with three children attached to it. They were surprised. So they helped them up and sent them to Hongxing (the name of a shipping company) for temporary lodging. They changed their wet clothes and gave them food. The three children drifted all night and were not injured at all. A large number of people came to see them after hearing the news. Everyone praised their miraculous escape. The three children were all very clever and eloquent. They calmly told people their names, family history, and the circumstances of their misfortune. Only then did they know that they had drifted as far as three hundred miles.

Reading Paintings at Luoyun Tower 185

— Rui Hongchu

The sultry heat is annoying, and staying at home is boring. I visited Mr. Zhang Linqiu's Luoyun Tower with my friend, Mr. Zhou Rongshang. Half of it is a collection room for ancient people's calligraphy and paintings, and the other half is Linqiu's personal works. Ancient paintings such as Zhao Ziang's "Water Goddess" and "Smoke Village Waiting for Ferry" have a carefree and leisurely atmosphere. I thought the most are from Qiu Shizhou, Tang Liuru, Li Longmian, and Shen Nantian. Among them, there is a horizontal scroll of "Pear Garden Incense Burning Night Celebration Picture". The layout is layered and orderly, and the brushwork is delicate and not weak. The delicate girl's melancholic expression can be vividly conveyed between the eyebrows. It is signed by Ms. Xue'e. I don't know who Xue'e is, so I asked Zhang. He said, "This is the daughter of my Zhang family's great-grandfather, Guan Yi. She married Sun Xiaolian Ziyangyue from Qiantang. This picture was made before she left the cabinet. After marriage, because she was busy managing the family, she abandoned painting, which is a pity." I also took a look at the calligraphy of Prince Chengqin, Qian Songtao, He Shaoji, Zhang Chuanshan, Liang Shanzhou, and Feng Guifen. They all created their own styles. I think the Zhang Wujin couplet is the oldest. From the Tang Dynasty to the present, the paper has not been greatly damaged, which shows the hard work of the collection. Then I went to Linqiu's personal works. Linqiu does not paint, but he writes ancient plum blossoms, snow plum blossoms, Jiaomei plums, Yingxi plums, and more than ten kinds of horizontal scroll hall pictures. And the brushwork is strange and strong, with a wild and unrestrained interest. Re-visiting his calligraphy, it is like entering the market of the five capitals, which is dazzling. Mr. Zhang's calligraphy can convey a sense of leisure and ease in the midst of vigor, so he has recently formed a wide range of ink friendships in Shanghai. (Couplets, halls, and other pieces only collect ink money of two yuan. Ruidai Hongchu of Minghua Store on Nanjing Road, Shanghai, collects them on behalf of them.) His reputation is full of the art world. When the sun set, I said goodbye and slowly walked back in the evening sun in the sound of cicadas. (No reward accepted)

Lady Fan's Dyke 186

— Yin Shouman

The Rongzi map in Jintan's northern town has a very high terrain, and it is adjacent to Tianhuang Dyke in the west. The river is the boundary between them. The map is high and the dyke is low, with a difference of five or six feet. Whenever it rains for a long time, the water in the map overflows into the dyke, and the fields and houses are all submerged. The people in the dyke have suffered from it more than once. Until the beginning of Guangxu, there was a rich widow named Fan in the town. She was old and had no children. She happened to hear about it and felt compassion for it. She then poured out half of her field property for the cost of building a dyke. It was managed and managed, and it was completed in three months. It was about eight feet wide and thirteen miles long. From then on, the dyke was saved from flooding. The people in the dyke felt her virtue and named it Lady Fan's Dyke. I admire Fan's enthusiasm for public welfare, so I recorded its beginning and end, so that those who read the writing can know that there are such people among women.

Announcement To Mr. Lü Bing: Please indicate your communication address. Send to the United Federation of Associations, No. 27 Beile Road, Shanghai.

Brief Letter I am visiting Chaozhou and Meizhou, lingering at sea, and eating irregularly. So I was affected by the frost and dew, and I suffered from the symptoms of pain in the four limbs. I could not turn around. I especially rushed to Shanghai to seek treatment from Dr. Sun Weicai of Ningbo Road in the French Concession. After Dr. Sun's several acupuncture needles, I was cured immediately. It is said that the disease is called acute rheumatic fever. People who live in warm and humid places or engage in water activities are often affected by this. It is not easy to cure with acupuncture. (Sincerely)

Miscellaneous Impressions of a Trip to Europe by Miss Yang Manhua (Part 2) 187

— Ping

The number of Chinese students studying in France is increasing year by year. The most popular subjects are law, political science, and economics. Presumably, these courses are easier than other sciences. Everyone wants to spend a few years getting a title, and then return home to become a university professor or get promoted and become rich. Getting a degree in France is not unusual. If you are willing to spend a few thousand francs upon graduation from the graduate school, you can hire a specialist to write a thesis for you. Then, you can hope to receive the honors of a doctorate or master's degree. It is said that those who study fine arts, like Xu Beihong, who put in a lot of hard work, are rare. As far as I (Miss Dang herself) know, sixty or seventy percent of the students studying in France are wasting their time. A bustling market like Paris, with everything so tempting, easily leads weak-willed people astray. Except for a few dedicated scholars, most students do not even struggle to escape this bad environment. They spend their time in debauchery, indulging in the flesh market, patronizing foreign prostitutes, and marrying foreign women, and so on. They almost forget their mission and the nation's great plan to cultivate talents. Furthermore, many self-funded students try every means to obtain public funds from the Boxer Indemnity to subsidize their tuition. In reality, they are not striving for this unexpected allowance for the sake of studying. On the contrary, it is the hardworking students who are truly dedicated to their studies who cannot share any of the benefits because they have no connections. That is the real hardship. In my personal opinion, students studying in France are indeed more romantic than those studying in other countries. I am not intentionally saying this out of prejudice. The situation of Japanese students in France, for example, is very different. Of course, Japan does not send as many students abroad as China does. Japanese students are diligent and hardworking. Unless it is to study a difficult subject and they specifically hire an expert to teach them, they will not hesitate to spend money, but otherwise, they never waste money. Therefore, Japanese students often make inventions and contributions in science after returning home, which is definitely not accidental success.

Whenever we go to any country in Europe, we always feel "ashamed of our inferiority" because our national power is weak and our international status is so pitifully low. I often wonder why Westerners are so arrogant when they come to China, while Chinese people become so dejected when they go to Europe. I cannot explain this feeling of "self-esteem" and "inferiority" myself. Not to mention ordinary people like us, even our diplomats are not as respected as foreign diplomats. This is really not surprising for diplomats, but the government does not care enough about the dignity of the country and does not understand the difficulties of diplomats. To say nothing else, just the funding for embassies and consulates abroad has been in arrears for months, leading to utter destitution. If an accident occurs and they need to report it to the central government, even the cost of a telegram can cause panic. Ordinary people think that diplomats are very rich, but those who have experienced it or know the details have long regarded diplomats as disaster officials and embassies and consulates as the poorest institutions.

Random Notes on a Northeast China Inspection Trip (6) 188

— Liu Suijiu

(X) The Fall of the Manchu Qing Dynasty Due to the "Ten Nos"

When we study the various undertakings operated by the Japanese in Northeast China, we must pay attention to the ideology, planning, and scientific methods of each undertaking. All undertakings must have ideological planning as a framework and scientific methods to promote their implementation in order to be effective. Some say that the Manchus were able to gain control of China because of Hong Chengchou's strategies, and that the fall of the Manchu Qing Dynasty was also due to the strategies planned by Hong. The great power of ideology is indeed profound, and cannot be understood by superficial materialists. After Hong Chengchou surrendered to the Qing, he greatly regretted his rash surrender at the time. In addition, Ming dynasty remnants set up altars to worship Hong Chengchou for sacrificing himself for the country, in order to provoke him. Hong then devised the "Ten Nos" strategy. The Qing court did not realize this and adhered to it generation after generation as ancestral family law. The ten nos are: (1) Men surrender, women do not. Men wear Manchu clothing, while women retain Han attire. (2) Officials surrender, servants do not. Officials use plumes and mandarin gowns, while servants still wear red and black hats and round-collared clothes, preserving the Han system. Officials are inferior to servants. (3) Civil officials surrender, military officials do not. Civil officials all wear Manchu attire, while military generals have a pavilion for armor, where armor is stored and paraded through the city when welcoming frost, greeting the god of joy, and displaying military might, to show that they do not forget the ancient system. (4) The old surrender, the young do not. People wear Qing clothes and hats when they reach adulthood, but at the beginning of life, the clothes in their swaddling clothes are all cut in the style of Taoist robes, and the hats are purple-gold crowns and crane scarves, all remnants of the Han ethnicity. (5) The living surrender, the dead do not. While alive, clothing and everything else勉强勉强 conform to Qing regulations, but after death, coffins, pillows, quilts, and other ornaments all follow the ancient Han customs. Moreover, filial sons wear mourning hats, carry mourning sticks, and wear hemp clothes and straw shoes, which are like a poem of the Ming dynasty, particularly striking and reminding people of the lost country. (6) Gentry, merchants, scholars surrender, beggars do not. In the past, during the Dragon Boat Festival and the New Year's Eve, some beggars would make paper gauze hats and dress up as Zhong Jinshi or the God of Wealth to beg for money from shops, allowing people to see the Han official ceremonies and stir up ethnic consciousness. (7) Secular families surrender, monks and nuns do not. Throughout the Qing dynasty, monks, Taoists, and nuns did not change their monastic robes. (8) Scholars of imperial examinations surrender, scholars who passed the county level exam do not. The "sparrow hats" and blue shirts are clearly of the Han system. (9) Officials of the living surrender, officials of the dead do not. Throughout the Qing dynasty, the city gods and land gods of each county and county all still wore gauze hats and red robes. (10) Heads surrender, feet do not. When officials paid tribute, they wore red-tasselled hats, though they were Qing officials, but they wore square-toed ancient boots. Hong Chengchou personally established the ten regulations, embedding the idea of ethnic revolution within them, while gradually weakening the Manchus. People are diligent in pursuing material things, but they have not considered the great power of ideology, which is enough to predetermine the fate of an entire nation. Genghis Khan's military advisor and Yuan dynasty Zhongshu Ling, Yelu Chucai, once met a Western Xia man named Chang Bajin who was good at making bows. Chang said to Chucai, "The country values military force, but you want to advance through literature. Isn't that the wrong way?" Chucai replied, "Bow makers still need craftsmen, so why shouldn't governing the world use the world's craftsmen?" In my study of the Northeast China problem, I deeply feel that the determination of ideological planning is more urgent than material construction.

Chinese Yarn Mills Buy Large Quantities of US Cotton 197

Imports of Indian Cotton Will Also Not Decrease Significantly

Since the sharp fall in US cotton prices, yarn mills have purchased more than 150,000 bales of US cotton in the last ten days. There have been fewer transactions in Indian cotton. Although this is due to the estimated increase in US cotton production, the price difference between US and Indian cotton has gradually become closer. Strictly speaking, the difference between the meter rate and the white cloth has been reduced to about 1 yuan 5 jiao in Japanese gold. Therefore, the low price of US cotton and the high price of Indian cotton have prompted Japanese factories to shift their strategy in spinning medium-count yarns. In the past, when spinning 20-count coarse yarn, the cotton mixing ratio was 80% Indian cotton and 20% US cotton. Now that the price difference has narrowed, the cotton mixing is bound to change. However, this will not affect the import of Indian cotton. Because of the reduced production of Hankou cotton due to disasters, in addition to being supplemented by Shandong and Tianjin cotton, which have better cotton production, it is still insufficient. Yarn mills use Chinese cotton and Indian cotton interchangeably. Now that Indian cotton is more expensive, inferior US cotton can be used as a substitute. Moreover, the trend in spinning is shifting to medium counts, so the import volume of US cotton is bound to increase.

Spot Yarn Shows a Clear Firming Trend 198

The cotton yarn market shows a firming trend. The overseas flower yarn situation has turned upwards, and the rise and fall have also shrunk, resulting in slightly better sentiment. However, the major sellers are calmly reluctant to replenish their positions, and there are many who are short due to the severe floods in various places, so the pressure is still heavy. Standard yarn was suspended for one day this month to handle deliveries, so there was less spot yarn business. There were fewer people gathering in the business premises in the afternoon, and there were very few open-market transactions. According to statistics, the various gangs only bought 300 bales throughout the day. The market was slightly firmer. Among the visiting gangs, Changsha entered 60 bales, Tianjin entered 60 bales, Guangdong entered 10 bales, the inland entered 45 bales, Sichuan entered 10 bales, the Northern gang entered 5 bales, and peers entered 100 bales. Standard cotton was suspended due to delivery, so there was no spot cotton business. However, the sentiment was firmer, because the US cotton was calm and the gold price was rising.

External Yarn Prices Without Major Fluctuations 199

American Cotton Weak Then Strong: Yesterday, American cotton initially weakened due to unfavorable news from Liverpool, but later strengthened due to purchases by Japanese merchants and short covering. Futures rose 8 to 12 points, and spot prices rose 10 points. British cotton futures were unchanged, while spot prices fell 3 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices fell 10 points. The Indian cotton market was calm and firm, with Pingor rising 0.5 rupees, Aumra rising 0.25 rupees, and Bai Luoxi rising 0.125 rupees. (Original telegram dated 28th)

Private Estimates of American Cotton 200

A telegram from New York on the 28th stated that the Clement Company estimates the production percentage at 67.1%, with a harvest of 15,512,000 bales. Their previous estimate was a production percentage of 70.6%, with a harvest of 13,981,000 bales.

Delay in New American Cotton Arrival 201

Suggestions for Cotton Field Management Likely to Fail

A telegram from New York on the 28th reported on the cotton market for the week, stating that at the beginning of the week, short covering was quite active due to increasing news of poor new cotton in the South. The result of maintaining market prices was uncertain, and hedging sales in the South were stagnant. The reason for the stagnation of hedging sales in the South is the delay in the arrival of new cotton. By the weekend, demand had turned sluggish, and market sentiment was awaiting developments. Although the legislative proposals for managing cotton fields have gained support from a state or two, it is generally expected that they will fail due to insufficient support. Currently, there are increasing complaints about the new cotton, making it difficult to predict the next government's estimate report. At the same time, short sellers hope that when new cotton arrives, hedging sales will increase, purchases will be limited, and low prices will make buyers cautious.

Grain: River-Bottom Rice Sales Slightly More Active 203

Yesterday in the South Market, sources from various groups were seen, about twenty-odd firms. Stocks in the Puxi area are also plentiful. Market sales were more active than the previous market. High-quality Changshu and Wuxi early indica rice was particularly stable; secondary quality moved as store sales gradually picked up. Sellers disposed of their goods with the market, and handling fees increased. Nearly a thousand dan from the same group was placed on the docks, and the situation looked promising with an increase of three chi. Sales of early and late rice were extremely brisk, and the situation stabilized. Sales of imported Luzhou long-grain rice were steady, and prices did not rise or fall. Discolored rice was sluggish at two yuan, with the price decreasing by ten cents.

Few sources on the Suzhou River bank in Xinzha, and buying interest from various suppliers was moderate. Sales of regular and Changzhou machine-processed rice were steady. Appetite for rice from Jiangyin and Kunshan was slight, with an increase of fifty cents. Incoming shipments of early and late rice were changing hands. Zou Zhuang's group handled three thousand shi, and the situation jumped sharply by seventy or eighty cents. Some imported pointed grain, pier grain, and Luzhou long-grain rice arrived, and buyer interest was very good. Prices were stable. The glutinous rice market lacked interest, discolored rice was very stagnant, and the price was short by half a chi. Purchases of imported rice by rice merchants tightened the situation. Cargo from river factories opened with about four thousand dan.

Starch Market Fluctuates Towards Stability 204

After the opening of the starch market yesterday morning and afternoon, the market for each month generally showed an image of initial fluctuation followed by stability. Because August is the last day of trading, it initially traded around one qian, and then fell to two liang and nine and a half fen. However, due to the low market price, distributors from the North and South roads found it profitable to package and sell, so they were gradually buying in. The quantity was estimated to be between seven and eight hundred thousand bags. Factories also automatically repurchased and hedged into subsequent months. Therefore, sentiment improved, and asking prices gradually increased, as the fact that this month could pass seemed to give a sense of security to those who went long. As a result, this month was up seven and a half li compared to the previous day, September was up five li, October was up one fen and two and a half li, November and December were up one fen, and January was up seven and a half li.

Wheat Market: Near and Far-Term Trends Differ 205

Yesterday's wheat futures market showed an image of near-term weakness and long-term stability. Since August has already passed, market sentiment for September was generally weak because most factories have abundant imported wheat in stock, and production is more than sufficient. If the quality is not cheap, they will mostly wait and see, and this is one reason for the recent weakness. The far-term market was slightly up because outsiders were slightly more optimistic, and sellers were less active. However, imported wheat prices remained poor, and the overseas situation had not yet escaped the state of oversupply. It is difficult to be overly optimistic about the future. As a result, September was down two fen compared to the previous day, October was down one fen, November was unchanged, December was up one fen, and January was up two fen. The current wheat market situation remains weak and sluggish. Yizheng wheat opened at three liang and six qian and two fen, Penglai wheat at three liang and seven qian, and Shahe wheat at three liang and six qian and a half, totaling over eight hundred bags, which was handled by Fuxin.

[P Foreign company customers are very sluggish, origin prices are high, telegrams not transferred]

Yesterday the imported rice market was flat, and telegrams were sent out by foreign firms, but because prices in the production areas were high, there was no response. The market was in a sluggish state, because importer appetites were very weak, and rice merchants had no interest. Local firms had goods arriving from the river bottom area, and only local firms were handling the transactions. Two firms sold 300 bags of Saigon rice at 13 yuan 8 jiao. There were no other transactions. Roll-over futures saw a small transaction of 300 tons in September at 6 liang and a half to 6 liang 5 qian 2 fen, similar to the previous market. As for the rumor that Bingchang Firm had newly purchased 200,000 "shun" in the production area, according to a letter from the firm, they stated that they did not purchase such a large amount, only a few thousand tons on behalf of customers.

Northern merchants have no interest in imported or locally produced goods, but are very welcome to local currency. They only dislike the lack of goods on the market, making it difficult to choose. Yesterday, only over one hundred bags of Zhongguan yuan were handled, priced at 14 yuan 2 jiao.

Sugar Market: Raw and White Sugar Trends Firmer 206

Taikoo Sugar Transactions Become More Active

Yesterday's sugar market production area telegrams: Cuban raw sugar price remains at 1.40625. New York futures: September 1.35, December 1.34, next year March 1.37, May 1.42. Compared to the previous telegram, near-term rebounded by four points, while the distant-term increased by one to two points. Java raw sugar price is 7.75, futures for all months are 7.625, unchanged from before. The Public Association market set prices. Although transactions of Dutch sugar No. 24 raw and white sugar are quiet, the market sentiment is quite strong. New goods are 11 liang 7 qian and a half, old goods are 11 liang 5 qian and a half. No. 20 high and medium raw and white sugar is 11 liang 2 qian, and No. 8 Dutch red sugar is 9 liang 5 qian, and No. 10 goods are 9 liang 7 qian. Market conditions are generally stable. Taikoo granulated sugar price settings have gradually become smoother, probably because demand from the North and inland Zhejiang province has slightly increased. B Mark's transaction price was 11 liang 9 qian 7 fen and a half, CW Mark 10 liang 9 qian, DY Mark 11 liang 8 qian, HM Mark 11 liang 4 qian, HX Mark 11 liang 7 qian, ○ Mark 9 liang 4 qian 2 fen and a half. The total transaction amount is estimated to be several thousand bags. There was a slight shortage of sellers, so the market outlook also showed some strength. Although inquiries for Ye Xin's No. 8 Dutch red sugar priced at 9 liang 5 qian were temporarily scarce, the market conditions were particularly firm.

North-South Goods: Orchid Seeds Open Down Four Liang 207

Recently, with genuine "water goods" of orchid seeds entering the market, prices have turned weak. It is heard that local conditions have suddenly caused wind and rain, resulting in four-tenths of the crop being blown down, and the arrival date has also been delayed. Yesterday's arrivals opened down about four liang. Because a large batch of goods will arrive in Shanghai in the later period, the trend is still turning soft. The future market will shift with the quantity of goods.
